Refutation of Christian Doctrines of Incarnation
The author refutes three Christian interpretations of the incarnation union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three Christian interpretations of the incarnation and the rational refutations against them.

Core Idea
The Christian concept of divine-human union is logically incoherent in all its forms.

This passage from a classical kalam work systematically refutes the Christian doctrine of the incarnation. The author presents three common interpretations of how divinity united with humanity in Jesus, and then demonstrates their impossibility through logical and conceptual analysis. As you read, notice how the refutation relies on necessary truths about essences, properties, and the nature of meanings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argumentative flow come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the three interpretations
The author mentions three interpretations of union: (1) union without separation, (2) mixture/blending, (3) impression. Find each one in the text.
Notice how the author introduces each with 'ومنهم من فسر' (among them are those who interpreted).
3
Understand the first refutation
The first claim is refuted by a necessary truth: one meaning cannot subsist in two essences. Ask yourself why this is self-evident.
4
Examine the refutations of mixture and impression
For mixture, the author argues that sensory mixture is a property of bodies, but the Word (Christ) is a meaning. For impression, he notes that only a likeness is produced, not the original itself.
5
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author ends with a strong condemnation, calling the doctrine irrational and the Christians intellectually deficient. Consider the rhetorical purpose of this language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثلاثة ، وهم يقولون : اتَّحد اللاهوتُ بناسوت عيسى عليهِ السلامُ مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يُفارِقَ ذات الجوهرِ ، ومِنَ المعلوم ضرورة : أنَّ المعنى الواحد لا يقوم بذاتين. ومنهم مَنْ فسَّرَ هذا الاتحاد بالاختلاط والمزج : كاختلاط الخمرِ مع الماء ونحوهما مِنَ المائعاتِ ، وكيف يُعقَلُ الاختلاط الحسي الذي هو مِنْ صفاتِ الأجسام في الكلمة التي هي معنى مِنَ المعاني ، بل هي حال عندهم وخاصيَّة للذات الأزليَّة ؟! ومنهم مَنْ فَسَّرَ الاتحاد بالانطباع : كانطباع صورة النقش في الشمع ، ومعلوم أنَّ نقش ذلك الشيء لم يحصل فيما طُبِعَ فيهِ ، وإِنَّما يحصل فيه مثاله . فانظر إلى هذا المذهب الركيكِ ما أخسَّهُ وأرذلَهُ ! وهو مذهب غيرُ معقول ، والنصارى أخسُّ الفِرَقِ كلّها وأرذلها أفهاماً ، وإدراك الحقائقِ على مثلهم عسير
The three, and they say: The divinity united with the humanity of Jesus, peace be upon him, without separating the essence of the substance, and it is known necessarily that one meaning cannot subsist in two essences. And among them are those who interpreted this union as mixture and blending: like the mixing of wine with water and similar liquids. How can sensory mixture, which is a property of bodies, be understood in the Word, which is a meaning among meanings, rather it is a state according to them and a property of the eternal essence?! And among them are those who interpreted the union as impression: like the impression of the image of an engraving in wax, and it is known that the engraving of that thing did not occur in what was impressed upon it, but rather its likeness occurs in it. So look at this feeble doctrine, how base and vile it is! It is an irrational doctrine, and the Christians are the basest of all sects and the most vile in understanding, and grasping realities is difficult for the likes of them.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian doctrines of the incarnation. The author first states the Christian claim that the divine nature (al-lāhūt) united with the human nature (an-nāsūt) of Jesus without separation of substance. He immediately refutes this by a necessary truth: one meaning cannot subsist in two essences. Then he presents two alternative interpretations: (1) union as mixture and blending, like wine and water; (2) union as impression, like an image in wax. He refutes the first by pointing out that sensory mixture is a property of bodies, but the Word (al-kalima) is a meaning, not a body. He refutes the second by noting that in impression, only a likeness of the original is produced, not the original itself. The passage concludes with a strong condemnation of these doctrines and a general dismissal of Christian intellectual capacity.

الناسوت
الاختلاط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'union' in Christian doctrine is a straightforward or coherent concept.
Correction: The author demonstrates that each interpretation (union without separation, mixture, impression) is logically flawed, thus the doctrine is rationally indefensible.

Checkpoint

A) The union is impossible because two natures cannot coexist.
B) One meaning cannot subsist in two essences.

Key Takeaway
The Christian doctrine of incarnation is rationally indefensible because each of its common interpretations violates necessary logical or conceptual principles.

Al-Razi's Logical Debate with a Christian Scholar
Imam al-Razi teaches a logical rule and uses it to disprove Jesus's divinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses a logical principle to refute the Christian claim of Jesus's divinity by showing that the same evidence would require Moses to be divine.

Core Idea
Evidence implies its conclusion, but absence of evidence is not absence of conclusion.

In this debate, Imam al-Razi first establishes a fundamental logical rule: that the existence of evidence necessarily proves the existence of its conclusion, but the absence of evidence does not disprove it. After securing agreement on this rule, he then applies it to the Christian argument for Jesus's divinity, leading to a powerful refutation. This narrative demonstrates how logical reasoning can be used to defend Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical rule
Read the first part of the passage where al-Razi teaches the Christian scholar a logical rule: evidence implies its conclusion, but absence of evidence does not imply absence of conclusion. Make sure you grasp this distinction.
The example of temporality (ḥudūth) and God's existence illustrates the rule.
2
Identify the Christian's claim
Read al-Razi's question and the Christian's response: why Jesus is considered divine because of his miracles. The Christian cites miracles like reviving the dead as evidence.
3
Apply the rule to Moses
Read how al-Razi applies the same rule to Moses, pointing out that Moses performed even greater miracles. Since evidence implies conclusion, Moses should also be divine. The Christian cannot deny because he already accepted the rule.
This is the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمامُ الفخرُ : ( ناظرتُ بعض أحبارهم، فوجدتُهُ في غاية البُعْدِ مِنَ المعقول، فعلَّمْتُهُ قاعدةً واحدةً مِنَ المعقول لأناظره بها؛ وهي أنَّ الدليل يلزمُ مِنْ وجودِهِ وجود المدلول، ولا يلزمُ مِنْ عدم الدليل عدمُ المدلول؛ كحدوثِ العالمِ مثلاً؛ فإنَّهُ دليل على وجودِ مولانا جل وعزَّ، فيلزمُ مِنْ وجودِ الحدوثِ وجود مدلوله الذي هو وجود مولانا جل وعزَّ، ولا يلزمُ مِنْ عدم الدليل ـ الذي هو الحدوث - عدم مدلوله الذي هو وجود مولانا تبارك وتعالى؛ فإنَّهُ كانَ الحدوث منفيّاً في الأزلِ، ووجود مولانا جل وعزَّ واجب في الأزلِ وواجب فيما لا يزالُ. فعَسُرَ عليهِ فهُمُ هذهِ القاعدة، فلم أزل معَهُ حتى فهمها وسلَّمَ لزومَ صِدْقِها، فقلتُ لهُ حينَئِذٍ : لِمَ خَصَصْتُمُ اتحاد أقنوم العلمِ بناسوتِ عیسی علیه السلام حتى جعلتموه إلها ؟ فقال لي : خصصنا بهِ الاتحادَ لِمَا ظهر على يديهِ مِنْ إحياء الموتى ونحوه ممَّا لا يقع إلا مِنَ الإله . فقلت له : يلزمكم أن تقولوا بألوهية موسى عليه السلام؛ لِمَا ظهر على يديهِ مِنْ إحياء العصا ثعباناً عظيماً، وفَلْقِ البحر أطواداً، ونحوِ ذلكَ ممّا يُقطَعُ أَنَّهُ ليسَ مِنْ فعل المخلوقِ ألبتة. فأرادَ أنْ ينكر، فقلتُ لهُ : قد سلَّمْتَ أَنَّهُ يلزمُ مِنْ وجودِ الدليل وجود المدلول، ودليل الوهيّة عيسى عليه السلام على زعمكم موجود في موسى عليه السلام، فيلزمُ أنْ يكونَ إلهاً مثلَهُ؛ لاستحالة وجودِ الدليل بدونِ المدلول.
Imam al-Fakhr said: I debated one of their scholars, and I found him extremely far from reason. So I taught him one logical principle by which to debate him: that from the existence of the evidence the existence of the evidence's conclusion necessarily follows, but from the non-existence of the evidence the non-existence of the conclusion does not necessarily follow. For example, the temporality of the world is evidence for the existence of our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted. So from the existence of temporality, the existence of its conclusion, which is the existence of our Lord, necessarily follows. But from the non-existence of the evidence—which is temporality—the non-existence of its conclusion, which is the existence of our Lord, may He be blessed and exalted, does not necessarily follow. For temporality was negated in pre-eternity, yet the existence of our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, was necessary in pre-eternity and necessary forever after. He found it difficult to understand this principle, so I kept at him until he understood it and conceded the soundness of its necessity. Then I said to him: Why did you specifically assign the union of the hypostasis of knowledge with the humanity of Jesus, peace be upon him, such that you made him a god? He said to me: We assigned the union to him because of what appeared at his hands—reviving the dead and the like—which cannot occur except from the divine. I said to him: It follows that you must assert the divinity of Moses, peace be upon him, because of what appeared at his hands—the transformation of the staff into a great serpent, the splitting of the sea into mountains, and the like—which is absolutely certain not to be the act of a created being. He tried to deny, so I said to him: You have already conceded that from the existence of the evidence the existence of the conclusion necessarily follows. The evidence for the divinity of Jesus according to your claim exists in Moses, so it follows that he must be a god like him, because it is impossible for the evidence to exist without the conclusion.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a narration of a debate between Imam al-Razi and a Christian scholar. Al-Razi first establishes a logical rule: that the presence of evidence necessarily implies the presence of its conclusion, but the absence of evidence does not imply the absence of the conclusion. He illustrates with the temporality of the world as evidence for God's existence. The scholar eventually accepts this rule. Then al-Razi asks why they specifically attribute union of the hypostasis of knowledge (the second person of the Trinity) to Jesus. The scholar answers: because of Jesus's miracles, which only God can do. Al-Razi then applies the rule: since the same kind of miracles were performed by Moses, and you accepted that evidence implies conclusion, then the same conclusion (divinity) must apply to Moses. When the scholar tries to deny, al-Razi reminds him that he already accepted the rule, and it is impossible for the evidence to exist without the conclusion. Thus, by parity of reasoning, the Christian claim is refuted.

Key Terms
الدليل
المدلول
الحدوث
الأزل
الأقنوم
الوهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles alone are sufficient proof that a person is divine.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that if miracles prove divinity, then Moses would also be divine, since he performed similar or greater miracles. Thus, miracles are not exclusive proof of divinity.

Checkpoint
What logical rule did al-Razi teach the Christian scholar before applying it to the debate?
A) Evidence is always necessary for a conclusion.
B) From the existence of evidence, the conclusion necessarily exists; from the absence of evidence, the conclusion does not necessarily cease.
C) Absence of evidence is evidence of absence.
D) The conclusion can exist without any evidence.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's logical rule shows that if evidence for divinity is claimed for Jesus, the same evidence for Moses would also require his divinity, thus refuting the Christian claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your faith do you claim evidence for something (e.g., a specific blessing, a sign of guidance) but would be unwilling to apply the same logical standard to another person or situation? Are you being consistent like al-Razi demands?
?
Al-Razi taught the Christian a logical rule before refuting him. Think of a time you argued about Islam: did you first establish common ground and principles, or did you jump to conclusions? How might you change your approach to reflect this example?
?
The Christian scholar accepted the rule but then tried to deny its application. When have you accepted a truth in theory but resisted its implications for your own beliefs or actions? Will you submit to the truth even when it challenges you?

The Shirk of Pre-Islamic Arabs: Misguided Reverence
Sanusi explains and refutes the shirk of pre-Islamic Arabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of shirk al-taqrib and the satanic reasoning behind the polytheism of pre-Islamic Arabs.

Core Idea
Pre-Islamic Arabs were not atheists; their shirk was misguided reverence.

This lesson examines a key form of shirk discussed by Sanusi: the shirk of drawing near (shirk al-taqrib). Pre-Islamic Arabs acknowledged God but considered direct worship disrespectful. The devil convinced them to worship intermediaries. Sanusi refutes this with a powerful court analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow: definition of shirk al-taqrib, the devil's whispering, and the analogy.
The passage contains a single coherent argument.
2
Identify the devil's argument
The devil whispered that direct worship by lowly humans is disrespectful. Find the phrase that describes this reasoning.
Look for 'تسويل الشيطان' and the content of his whisper.
3
Understand the refutation analogy
Sanusi uses an analogy from worldly courts: bypassing ministers to approach the king directly is discourteous. How does this refute the devil's argument?
The analogy shows that the pre-Islamic Arabs' reasoning is actually a satanic deception, not true reverence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا شِرْكُ التقريب الذي دانَ بهِ مُتقدِّمو الجاهلية : فشبهتهم الحاملة لهم على ذلكَ : تسويلُ الشيطان لهم ؛ أن وسوس لهم : إنَّ عبادتكم للمولى العظيم على ما أنتم عليهِ مِنْ غاية الضعف والدناءة والعجزِ والمهانة (۳) ، وترككم التقرُّبَ إِليهِ بعبادةِ مَنْ هو أعلى منكم عندَهُ وأشرفُ وأقوى ؛ كالملائكة والشمس والقمر والنجوم والنار ونحوها . . سوء أدب عظيم . ألا ترى في الشاهد : أن تخطي الأدنى الحقير جداً خدمة الحاكم والقائدِ والمزوار (۱) والوزير ونحوهم ممَّنْ هو شريف عند الملكِ ؛ إلى مباشرة خدمة الملكِ ابتداءً . . سوء أدب على الملكِ ؛ لما فيهِ مِنْ تجاسر الحقير على القُربِ منهُ ، وعدم مراعاة هيبته وعظمته بالتوسل إليهِ مِنْ بُعْدِ بمَنْ يمكنه التوصُّلُ إلى خدمتِهِ مِنْ أعوانه وخواص مماليكه ؟!
As for the shirk of approach (shirk al-taqrib) which the earlier Jahiliyyah practiced: their pretext that led them to that was the devil's whispering to them, as he whispered to them: 'Your worship of the Mighty Master, given your extreme weakness, baseness, incapacity, and lowliness, and your refraining from drawing near to Him by worshipping one who is higher than you in His sight, more noble and stronger—like the angels, the sun, the moon, the stars, the fire, and the like—is a great discourtesy. Do you not see in the empirical world that bypassing the lowly, contemptible person to serve the ruler, the leader, the governor, the vizier, and others who are honorable with the king, and going directly to serve the king from the outset, is a discourtesy to the king? Because it contains the impertinence of the contemptible person to draw near to him, and not observing his awe and majesty by seeking intercession from afar through those of his aides and special servants who can reach his service?'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage explains the rationale behind the shirk of pre-Islamic Arabs, called 'shirk al-taqrib' (the shirk of drawing near). They believed that directly worshipping God without intermediaries was disrespectful due to human lowliness. The devil whispered that they should instead worship higher beings (angels, celestial bodies, etc.) to gain proximity to God. The author refutes this by an analogy: in worldly court, approaching the king directly is disrespectful; one should approach through his ministers. Thus the Jahiliyyah saw their idolatry as reverence, but it was a satanic deception.

Key Terms
شرك التقريب
التقرّب
الوسوسة
الشيطان
سوء الأدب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Pre-Islamic Arabs were atheists or denied the existence of God.
Correction: They acknowledged God but believed direct worship was disrespectful, so they worshipped intermediaries to draw near to Him—a form of shirk called shirk al-taqrib.

Checkpoint
What was the devil's argument to justify shirk among the pre-Islamic Arabs?
A) Allah is unjust and requires appeasement.
B) Direct worship of Allah by lowly humans is a discourtesy, so they should worship higher beings to get closer.
C) Idols are themselves gods worthy of worship.
D) Worship of multiple gods is more efficient than one.

Key Takeaway
Shirk al-taqrib is the error of thinking direct worship of God is disrespectful, leading to idolatry through satanic deception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your sins make you too unworthy to pray directly to Allah, and that you need some 'intermediary' to make your worship acceptable? How does Sanusi's refutation of shirk al-taqrib expose that feeling as a deception of Shaytan? What will you do the next time this whisper occurs?
?
In what areas of your life do you show 'su' al-adab' (bad manners) by making excuses to avoid direct obedience to Allah—such as delaying prayer, being careless in worship, or rationalizing sins? This lesson reveals that true adab is to approach Allah directly with humility. What specific change will you make today to correct one such area?
?
The pre-Islamic Arabs thought they were honoring God by worshipping intermediaries, but they were actually committing shirk. Are there any 'intermediaries' in your life—people, status, wealth, or even good deeds—that you rely on more than you rely on Allah's direct mercy? How can you practically redirect your trust to Allah alone, starting today?

Origin of Idol-Making in Pre-Islamic Arabia
Sanusi describes the origin of idol-making among the pre-Islamic Arabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's explanation of how idol-making originated among pre-Islamic Arabs and why he considers it a form of misguidance.

Core Idea
Idolatry began as a misguided attempt to worship God through representations of absent beings.

Sanusi presents a historical and theological account of how idol-making began. He argues that it stemmed from the absence of worshipped beings (angels, celestial bodies, Jesus) and the human desire to maintain a physical focus for worship. However, he condemns this practice as a satanic deception, emphasizing that all created things are equally dependent on God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the sequence of reasoning: cause (absence), response (idol-making), intention (proximity to God), and evaluation (misguidance).
2
Identify the beings worshipped
List the beings mentioned: angels, sun, moon, stars, Jesus. Note that some are permanently absent (angels), others temporally absent (celestial bodies, Jesus).
This sets the context for why idols were needed.
3
Understand the purpose of idol-making
Sanusi states that idols were made as 'examples' (أمثلة) of absent beings, and worship was directed ultimately to God through them. This is key to his critique.
Contrast with modern misconceptions that they were worshipped as gods directly.
4
Reflect on Sanusi's condemnation
He calls it clear misguidance (ضلالة) and devilish deception. His final point is that all creation is equally incapable and in need of God, so no created thing deserves worship.
This is the theological punchline.
5
Complete the checkpoint activity
Answer the multiple-choice question to test your understanding of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما رأى بعضُهم غَيبةَ مَنِ اختار عبادته وخدمته عنه (۲) ؛ إِمَّا دائماً ؛ كالملائكةِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ ، أو في بعض الأوقاتِ ؛ كالشمس والقمر والنجوم وعيسى عليه السلام . . صنعوا الأصنام أمثلةً لِمَا عَابَ عنهم مِنْ معبوداتهم ، ولازموا عبادتها ، والتقرب إليها بالذبح والأموال ، ونيَّتُهمُ التقرُّبُ بذلك لما جُعِلَتْ مثالاً له ، والقصد مِنَ الجميعِ أن يتقرَّبوا إلى المولى العظيم تبارك وتعالى ! ولا خفاء في ضلالتهم ، وتلاعب الشيطان اللعين بعقولهم ، نسألُ الله تعالى السلامة والعافية بمنّه . ولو تنبهوا أدنى تنبه لعلموا استواء جميع ميع العوالم ؛ علويها وسفليّها ، مظلمها ومضيئها ، قويّها وضعيفها .. في العجز والافتقار
Then when some of them saw the absence of those whom they had chosen to worship and serve—either always, like the angels (peace be upon them), or at certain times, like the sun, moon, stars, and Jesus (peace be upon him)—they made idols as likenesses of those objects of worship that were absent from them, and they persisted in worshipping them, and drawing near to them by slaughtering animals and spending wealth, while their intention was to draw near thereby to the one for whom the idol was made a likeness. And the purpose of all that was to draw near to the Mighty Master, Blessed and Exalted! And there is no concealment of their misguidance, and the devil's tampering with their minds. We ask Allah Almighty for safety and well-being by His grace. And if they had paid the slightest attention, they would have known the equality of all the worlds—their upper and lower, dark and luminous, strong and weak—in incapacity and neediness.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage explains how idol-making originated. When the beings they worshipped (angels, celestial bodies, Jesus) were absent—whether permanently (angels) or temporarily (sun, moon, stars, Jesus)—they created physical idols as representations to focus their worship. They continued these rituals with the intention of gaining proximity to God through these representations. The author condemns this as clear misguidance and devilish deception. He notes that if they had reflected, they would realize all created things are equally powerless and in need of God, thus unworthy of worship.

Key Terms
الأصنام
أمثلة
الغيبة
التقرّب
الضلالة
العجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That pre-Islamic idol worshippers believed the idols themselves were gods.
Correction: According to Sanusi, they made idols as representations of other beings (angels, celestial bodies, Jesus) and intended to draw near to God through them. They did not consider the idols to be divine in themselves.

Checkpoint
What reason does Sanusi give for why pre-Islamic Arabs began making idols?
A) They believed idols were gods themselves.
B) They wanted to create art for worship.
C) The beings they worshipped were often absent, so they made likenesses to focus their worship.
D) Satan commanded them to carve statues.

Key Takeaway
Idolatry originated from a misguided attempt to worship God through representations of absent beings, but all created things are equally dependent on God and thus unworthy of worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever crafted a ‘likeness’ in your heart—an image, a habit, or even a person—that you held as a means to feel closer to God, only to realize it became a veil? What is it, and will you let it go now to face Him directly?
?
The idolaters thought they were worshipping God through their objects. In what subtle ways do you reduce worship to a ritual or object, forgetting the living, all-powerful God who needs no representation? Name one thing you rely on more than God. Will you repent and return to pure reliance today?
?
Sanusi says if they had paid the slightest attention, they would have seen that all creation is equal in neediness. When you look at your own life, where do you attribute power or independence to something other than God? What would change if you truly believed that nothing besides Him deserves your trust? Will you take one step today to uproot that false dependency?

The Unanimous Message of All Prophets on Tawheed
Sanusi declares the unanimous consensus of all prophets on tawheed and the consequence of shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all prophets from Adam to Muhammad unanimously taught tawheed as the core obligation and warned that those who die upon shirk will suffer eternal punishment.

Core Idea
All prophets agreed: worship Allah alone; shirk leads to eternal loss.

Sanusi opens this lesson by establishing the universal consensus of all prophets on the central Islamic message. This agreement is not merely historical but serves as a decisive proof that shirk is the greatest sin and that no human excuse can justify it. Let's explore this foundational statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm, then read the translation. Notice the authoritative tone: 'have unanimously agreed'.
The passage uses strong language: 'أطبقت' (agreed) and 'أجمعوا' (unanimously).
2
Identify the three elements
The passage contains: (1) the consensus of prophets, (2) the obligation of tawheed and prohibition of shirk, (3) the consequence for those who die on shirk. List them.
3
Reflect on the severity
The punishment is described as 'محروم من جميع نعم الآخرة' (deprived of all blessings of the Hereafter) and 'مخلد في العذاب العظيم إلى غير نهاية' (eternally abiding in the great punishment). Think about why this is so severe.
This shows that shirk is the only unforgivable sin if unrepented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أطبقتْ رُسُلُ المولى تبارك وتعالى وأجمعوا كلُّهم ، مِنْ لَدُنْ آدم عليه السلام إلى خاتم النبيِّينَ وسيّد المرسلين نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .. على أنَّ الله سبحانَهُ كلَّفَ عبيده بتوحيدِهِ ، وحرَّمَ عليهم التشريكَ في الوهيَّه وعبادتِهِ ، وبلغوا عن المولى تبارك وتعالى أنَّ مَنِ ابْتُلِيَ بهذا المحرَّم ؛ وهو الشرك في الألوهية والعبادة ، ومات على ذلك.. فهو محرومٌ مِنْ جَميعِ نِعَمِ الآخرةِ ، مُخلَّدٌ في العذاب العظيم إلى غير نهاية . وإذا نظرت إلى شبهة هؤلاء الذين أشركوا بالتقريب . . وجدتها غير مقتضية للشركِ ، وإِنَّما تقتضي مُجرَّدَ التقرب إلى الملكِ بمَنْ . قال العلامة الإمام السعد التفتازاني في ( شرح العقائد النسفية ) ( ص ٢١٢ ) : ( الإشراك : هو إثبات الشريك في الألوهية ؛ بمعنى : وجوب الوجود كما للمجوس ، أو بمعنى : استحقاق العبادة كما لعبدة الأصنام ) ، وأنت تعلم أنَّ معنى التوسل في نفسه لا يشتمل على أحد هذين المعنيين ؛ لأن حقيقة الشرك في إثبات خاصية من خواص الإله لغيره من المخلوقات ؛ كما يقول المصنف في شرح الجزائرية » ( ص ١٥٦ ) ، ولكن فصَّلُوا القول في بعض المسائل ؛ كإثبات القدرة الفاعلة للحادث عند المعتزلة ، فلم يقولوا بكفرهم على أصح القولين
And the messengers of the Lord, Blessed and Exalted is He, have unanimously agreed, all of them, from Adam, peace be upon him, to the Seal of the Prophets and the Master of the Messengers, our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that Allah, Exalted is He, obligated His servants to worship Him alone (tawheed) and prohibited them from associating partners (shirk) in divinity and worship. And they conveyed from the Lord, Blessed and Exalted is He, that whoever is afflicted with this forbidden thing—i.e., shirk in divinity and worship—and dies upon that, then he is deprived of all the blessings of the Hereafter, eternally abiding in the great punishment without end. And if you look at the specious argument of those who commit shirk by way of seeking nearness (taqrib), you find it does not necessitate shirk; rather, it necessitates mere seeking nearness to the King through someone. Al-Allama al-Imam Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani said in (Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya) (p. 212): 'Shirk is the affirmation of a partner in divinity, either in the sense of necessity of existence, as with the Majus, or in the sense of deserving worship, as with the idol worshippers.' And you know that the meaning of tawassul (seeking intercession) in itself does not include either of these two meanings, because the reality of shirk is the affirmation of a characteristic among the characteristics of the divine for someone other than Him from among created beings, as the author says in Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya (p. 156). But they have elaborated the discussion on some issues, such as affirming effective power for originated events among the Mu'tazila, but they did not declare them disbelievers according to the sounder of the two opinions.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a combined statement of the unanimous teaching of all prophets on tawheed and a refutation of the justification for shirk. It begins by asserting that all messengers from Adam to Muhammad concurred that Allah obligated tawheed and forbade shirk in divinity and worship. They conveyed that whoever commits shirk and dies upon it will be eternally deprived of the blessings of the Hereafter and abiding in punishment. Then it addresses a specious argument (shubha) of those who commit shirk claiming they are only seeking nearness (taqrib) to Allah through intermediaries. The author examines this and finds that their logic does not actually necessitate shirk but only mere seeking nearness to the King through someone. He then supports this by quoting al-Taftazani's definition of shirk: affirming a partner in divinity either in necessary existence (as dualists) or in deserving worship (as idolaters). The author notes that tawassul (seeking intercession) does not imply either meaning because shirk is really about attributing a specific divine characteristic to a creature. He references the author of Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya. Finally, he mentions that scholars have discussed some borderline cases like the Mu'tazila affirming originated effective power, but they did not declare them disbelievers according to the sounder opinion. This clarifies that the shirk being discussed is major shirk (associating partners in divinity), not minor issues.

Key Terms
أطبقت
أجمعوا
توحيد
شرك
مخلد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that only certain prophets taught tawheed or that shirk is not that severe.
Correction: Sanusi emphasizes that all prophets without exception taught tawheed, and shirk leads to eternal punishment.

Checkpoint
What happens to a person who dies upon shirk according to the unanimous message of the prophets?
A) They will be punished temporarily and then enter Paradise.
B) They are deprived of all blessings of the Hereafter and abide eternally in great punishment.
C) They will be resurrected as disbelievers but eventually forgiven.
D) They will be given a chance to repent in the grave.

Key Takeaway
The unanimous message of all prophets is that tawheed is obligatory and shirk is a sin that leads to eternal punishment if unrepented.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all prophets from Adam to Muhammad agreed on the absolute necessity of tawheed and the prohibition of shirk, what does that say about the seriousness of any form of shirk in your own life, even subtle ones like showing off (riya) or trusting fully in created means? Are there any actions or intentions where you are effectively associating partners with Allah without realizing it? Commit to identifying one such area and repent today.
?
The passage states that dying upon shirk means eternal deprivation from all blessings of the Hereafter. Do you truly believe that? If so, how does it change your daily priorities? What are you actively doing to ensure you die upon tawheed? Write one concrete action you will take this week to strengthen your tawheed.

Refuting the Excuse of Seeking Nearness (Taqrib)
Sanusi refutes the excuse of using intermediaries and defines shirk via Taftazani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that seeking intercession (tawassul) is not shirk, and that shirk is specifically defined as attributing divine attributes (such as necessary existence or deserving worship) to others.

Core Idea
Seeking nearness to Allah through a righteous person is not shirk; shirk is attributing divine properties to others.

Some polytheists argue that they only seek nearness to Allah through their idols or saints, not that they are divine themselves. Sanusi refutes this by examining their logic: seeking nearness does not require shirk. He then quotes al-Taftazani to provide a precise definition of shirk: affirming a partner in divinity either in necessary existence or in worship. This helps distinguish tawassul from actual shirk.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the shubha
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the specious argument (shubha) of those who commit shirk by claiming they only seek nearness.
The shubha is that they claim their actions are just 'taqrib' (seeking nearness).
2
Analyze Taftazani's definition of shirk
Al-Taftazani defines shirk as affirming a partner in al-uluhiyya (divinity) in two senses: wujub al-wujud (necessary existence) or istihqaq al-ibada (deserving worship). Understand these two meanings.
This definition is key to understanding what really constitutes shirk.
3
See how tawassul differs
The passage says that tawassul (seeking intercession) does not include either meaning. Reflect on why tawassul is not shirk.
Tawassul is asking a righteous person to pray for you, not worshipping them.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to al-Taftazani as quoted in the passage, what are the two meanings of shirk?

B) Affirming a partner in divinity in the sense of necessary existence or deserving worship.
C) Associating partners in creation and provision.
D) Worshipping others besides Allah in any form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever performed an action seeking closeness to Allah through a righteous person, but without fully examining your intention? Ask yourself: did you, even for a moment, attribute any independent power to that person to bring you near? This lesson shows that shirk includes considering another as necessarily existent. Could your tawassul contain a hidden attribution of necessity? Commit to purifying your intention so that all reliance is solely on Allah.
?
When you are in desperate need—facing illness, poverty, or fear—do you ever mentally elevate the means (a doctor, a leader, a saint) to the point where you feel their power is beyond what Allah has granted? The definition of shirk from Taftazani warns that affirming a partner in necessity of existence is shirk. Reflect on your moments of panic: is your trust truly in Allah alone? What concrete step will you take to recenter your tawakkul on Allah exclusively?
?
This lesson notes that scholars did not declare the Mu'tazila disbelievers despite their serious error about divine attributes. Are you quick to label other Muslims as disbelievers over disagreements in theology or practice? Does this caution humble you? Before making any takfir, do you seek to understand the person's actual belief? Challenge yourself: next time you encounter a theological difference, pause and apply the restraint shown here. How can you cultivate that same carefulness?

Polytheism of Imitation: Causes and Warning
Sanusi defines shirk al-taqlid, states its causes, and condemns it as destructive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of shirk al-taqlid, its root causes according to Sanusi, and why it is a blameworthy form of polytheism.

Core Idea
Blind imitation of ancestors in falsehood is driven by desire and foolishness, not ignorance.

In this passage, Sanusi turns from discussing types of shirk to focus on a particularly insidious form: shirk al-taqlid, or polytheism born from blind imitation. He identifies the psychological and social causes that lead people to persist in ancestral falsehood despite clear evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the definition and the three causes listed.
The passage is dense; take your time to parse each phrase.
2
Identify the three causes
Find the words for desire (الهوى), foolishness (الحمق), and partisanship (التعصب). Reflect on how each contributes to shirk al-taqlid.
Sanusi groups these as psychological and social factors.
3
Analyze the reflective argument
Sanusi says if they reflected even a little, they would see the foolishness. Ask yourself: why does he emphasize this? What does it imply about their responsibility?
This shows that the error is not due to lack of evidence but willful disregard.
4
Consider the ruling
Based on the passage, is shirk al-taqlid excusable? What does the cause (desire, foolishness, partisanship) imply about its severity?
The passage clearly condemns it as destructive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرك التقليد وبيان حكمه: وأما شرك التقليد: فسببه غلبة الهوى، والحمق، والتعصب للآباء والأجداد في متابعتهم على الباطل وأسباب الهلاك في العاجل والآجل(٢)، ولو تأملوا أدنى تأمل لقاسوا هذا الحمق الموجب للهلاك الذي وقع فيه آباؤهم وأجدادهم؛ من الشرك بالله تعالى في ألوهيته وعبادته، وتكذيبهم رسله عليهم الصلاة والسلام بعد شهادة (٢) في (أ) وحدها: (والحمق بالتعصب) بدل (والحمق، والتعصب)، وقد مثل لهذا الشرك بشرك متأخري الجاهلية.
Polytheism of imitation and explanation of its ruling: As for polytheism of imitation, its cause is the dominance of desire, foolishness, and partisanship for fathers and grandfathers in following them upon falsehood and the causes of destruction in the immediate and the later (2). And if they reflected with the slightest reflection, they would consider this foolishness that necessitates destruction which their fathers and grandfathers fell into: from polytheism with God Almighty in His divinity and worship, and their denial of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, after [their] testimony. (2) In (A) alone: (and foolishness through partisanship) instead of (and foolishness, and partisanship), and he gave an example of this polytheism with the polytheism of the later Jahiliyyah.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage defines shirk al-taqlid (polytheism of imitation) and explains its ruling. The author states that its cause is the predominance of desire (hawa), foolishness (hamaq), and partisanship (ta'assub) for ancestors, leading to following them upon falsehood and causes of destruction in this world and the next. If such people reflected even minimally, they would realize the foolishness of their ancestors' polytheism in denying God's divinity and worship and rejecting His messengers after clear testimony. The footnote notes a textual variant and mentions that an example of this is the polytheism of the later Jahiliyyah. The passage thus identifies the root cause of imitative polytheism and condemns it as destructive.

Key Terms
شرك التقليد
الهوى
الحمق
التعصب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People commit shirk al-taqlid because they are ignorant and have no access to the truth.
Correction: Sanusi shows the cause is not ignorance but willful desire, foolishness, and stubborn partisanship. Minimal reflection would reveal the error, so it is blameworthy.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary cause of shirk al-taqlid?
A) Lack of access to knowledge
B) Dominance of desire, foolishness, and partisanship for ancestors
C) External coercion
D) Misinterpretation of scripture

Key Takeaway
Shirk al-taqlid stems from willful desire and partisanship, not ignorance, thus rendering it inexcusable and destructive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you defend a religious practice simply because it is what your family or community does, have you paused to examine whether it is based on the Quran and Sunnah? What desire or partisanship might be preventing you from seeing the truth if it differs?
?
Sanusi calls imitating ancestors in falsehood 'foolishness that necessitates destruction.' Is there any belief or action you hold onto out of attachment to your upbringing, even after evidence has been presented against it? What would it cost you to let it go?
?
If you were to reflect deeply on your religious practices, which one would you be most afraid to question? Why does that fear exist, and could it be rooted in the very partisanship this passage warns against?

The Six Types of Shirk and Their Rulings
Sanusi enumerates the six types of shirk and their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rulings for the six types of shirk as classified by Sanusi, and the distinction between the fifth type's two subcases.

Core Idea
Not all shirk is kufr; the fifth type has a detailed ruling depending on the belief about causal efficacy.

Sanusi presents a precise classification of shirk into six types, each with a specific ruling. The first four are unanimously kufr, the sixth is sin without kufr, and the fifth requires careful distinction. This passage lays out the consensus and the two possible views on causation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the six types
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the three categories: first four, fifth, sixth.
The fifth type is the only one with detail.
2
Understand the two subcases of the fifth type
Identify the difference between attributing effect to nature vs. to a power deposited by God.
The first subcase is kufr by consensus; the second is fisq with two opinions.
3
Connect to larger framework
Realize that this classification is foundational for judging beliefs about causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم القائلين بأنواع الشرك الستة ] وَحُكْمُ الْأَرْبَعَةِ الأُولِ : الْكُفْرُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ، وَحُكْمُ السَّادِسِ : الْمَعْصِيَةُ مِنْ غَيْرِ كُفْرٍ بِإِجْمَاعِ ، وَحُكْمُ الْخَامِسِ : التَّفْصِيلُ ؛ فَمَنْ قَالَ فِي الْأَسْبَابِ الْعَادِيَّةِ : إِنَّهَا تُؤَثُرُ بِطَبْعِهَا .. فَقَدْ حُكِيَ الإجْمَاعُ عَلَى كُفْرِهِ ، وَمَنْ قَالَ : إِنَّهَا تُؤَكِّرُ بِقُوَّةٍ أَوْدَعَهَا الله تَعَالَى فِيهَا .. فَهُوَ فَاسِقٌ مُبْتَدِعٌ ، وَفِي كُفْرِهِ قَوْلانِ . حكمُ الآخذ بالأنواع الأربعةِ الأُولِ ] مراده بالأربعةِ الأُولِ : كفرُ الاستقلال، وكفرُ التبعيض ، وكفرُ التقريب ، وكفرُ التقليد (١) ، ولم يجعل الشرع التأويل ولا التقليد في الكفر الصريح عذراً لصاحبه (۲) ؛ لإمكان معرفة الخطأ فيه بأدنى نظر في (۳) (۱) عبَّرَ هنا بالكفر ولم يعبر بالشرك كما عبّر به فيما تقدم ؛ لأن الكفر لازم للشرك هذه الأربعة ، وأما الشرك والكفر مطلقاً فلا يفيد هذه الأربعة ، فبينهما عموم وخصوص من وجه ؛ يجتمعان في الأربعة ، وينفرد الشرك في شرك الأغراض ، وينفرد الكفر في الإيجاب الذاتي (۲) التأويل للثلاثة الأول ، والتقليد خاص بالرابع ، وهذا مقابل بما سيأتي من قبول التأويل والاجتهاد فيما سيأتي (۳) انظر ما تقدم ( ص ١٧٤ ) ، وينبني على إثبات كفر هذه الأنواع الأربعة : عدم المغفرة لهم ، وعدم دخولهم الجنة ، والخلود في النار ، كذا ذكر العلامة البناني في شرحه للمقدمات ) ( ص ۳۱ ) ، وسيأتي مزيد تفصيل في ذلك
The ruling of those who profess the six types of shirk. The ruling of the first four is unbelief by consensus, and the ruling of the sixth is disobedience without unbelief by consensus, and the ruling of the fifth is detailed. So whoever says concerning ordinary causes that they have effect by their nature, then consensus has been reported on his unbelief. And whoever says that they have effect by a power which God Most High has deposited in them, then he is a transgressor and an innovator, and concerning his unbelief there are two sayings. The ruling of one who adopts the first four types. What he means by the first four is: the unbelief of independence, the unbelief of partiality, the unbelief of drawing near, and the unbelief of imitation. And the Law has not made interpretation nor imitation in explicit unbelief an excuse for its practitioner (2), because of the possibility of knowing the error therein with minimal reflection in (3). (1) He expressed here with 'unbelief' and did not express with 'shirk' as he did previously, because unbelief is necessary for these four types of shirk. But shirk and unbelief in absolute terms do not yield these four types, so between them is generality and specificity in some respect: they meet in the four, and shirk is specific in the shirk of purposes, and unbelief is specific in self-obligation. (2) Interpretation for the first three, and imitation specifically for the fourth, and this contrasts with what will come of accepting interpretation and ijtihad in what follows. (3) See what preceded (p. 174), and upon establishing the unbelief of these four types depends: lack of forgiveness for them, their not entering Paradise, and eternal abiding in the Fire. Thus mentioned al-'Allama al-Bannani in his commentary on 'al-Muqaddimat' (p. 31), and further detail will come on that.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage provides the rulings for the six types of shirk and then clarifies the four types of kufr. Sanusi begins by stating the ruling of the first four types of shirk: they are unbelief (kufr) by consensus. The sixth type is disobedience without unbelief by consensus. The fifth type requires detail: if someone claims that ordinary causes (like fire burning) have effect by their own nature, then consensus holds that this is unbelief. If, however, they claim that these causes act by a power that God has placed in them, then the person is a transgressor (fasiq) and an innovator (mubtadi'), and there are two opinions regarding his unbelief. Then Sanusi specifies the first four types of kufr: kufr al-istiqlal (unbelief of independence, ascribing independent power to other than God), kufr al-tab'id (unbelief of partiality, ascribing some power to other than God while acknowledging God), kufr al-taqrib (unbelief of drawing near, performing acts to draw near to other than God), and kufr al-taqlid (unbelief of imitation, blindly following others in shirk). The Law does not accept ta'wil (interpretation) nor taqlid (imitation) as an excuse for explicit unbelief, because the error can be known with minimal reflection. The passage includes scholarly notes: the author explains his terminology—he uses 'kufr' here rather than 'shirk' because kufr is necessary for these four types of shirk, though in general shirk and kufr have overlap; and he notes that ta'wil applies to the first three types, while taqlid is specific to the fourth. Finally, he mentions that establishing these four types as kufr entails denial of forgiveness, prohibition from Paradise, and eternity in Hell, as noted by al-Bannani, with further detail to come.

Key Terms
شرك
كفر
أسباب عادية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all shirk is necessarily kufr.
Correction: The sixth type is sin without kufr, and the fifth type's second subcase is not necessarily kufr.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the ruling on the fifth type of shirk if one says causes act by a power God deposited in them?
A) Kufr by consensus
B) Fisq and innovation with two opinions on kufr
C) Sin without kufr
D) Permissible

Key Takeaway
The sixth type of shirk is only sin, not kufr, while the fifth type's ruling depends on the belief about causal efficacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a natural event, do you immediately think of its physical cause without consciously acknowledging that God is the ultimate Creator and the One who gives that cause its effect? How does this lesson expose a subtle shirk in your heart? Take a moment to repent and renew your tawheed.
?
Have you ever attributed any success or failure solely to your own effort or to external factors, forgetting that Allah alone is the true agent? This lesson forces you to examine your daily thoughts on causality. Will you discipline your mind to see every cause as a mere vessel for Allah's power?
?
If someone told you that believing causes act by a power God placed in them is a lesser form of shirk, would you dismiss it as unimportant? But this lesson shows it is fisq and innovation with possible kufr. Does your heart take such matters seriously, or do you brush off fine points of aqeedah? Commit to studying and guarding your belief in Allah's sole effectiveness.

The Four Types of Kufr and the Inadmissibility of Excuses
Sanusi specifies the four types of kufr and their consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four specific types of kufr that Sanusi identifies from among the six types of shirk, and why ta'wil and taqlid are not accepted as excuses for explicit kufr.

Core Idea
Ta'wil and taqlid do not excuse explicit kufr because error is knowable with minimal reflection.

After detailing the rulings on the six shirk types, Sanusi specifies the first four as distinct types of kufr. He then explains that neither interpretive reasoning nor blind imitation can excuse someone from the charge of kufr when the matter is clear, and he highlights the grave consequences of falling into these four types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of kufr
Read the list: kufr al-istiqlal, kufr al-tab'id, kufr al-taqrib, kufr al-taqlid.
Note that these correspond to the first four shirk types.
2
Understand the rule on excuses
Sanusi states that ta'wil and taqlid are not valid excuses for explicit kufr because the error can be known with minimal reflection.
This is a key point against relativistic interpretations of takfir.
3
Grasp the consequences
The footnote mentions that establishing these four as kufr entails no forgiveness, no Paradise, and eternal Fire.
This underscores the severity.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi state that the Law does not accept ta'wil or taqlid as excuses for explicit kufr?
A) Because the person is a fasiq and mubtadi'
B) Because the error can be known with minimal reflection
C) Because ta'wil is always invalid in matters of kufr
D) Because taqlid is forbidden for everyone

Key Takeaway
The first four types of shirk are categorized as specific types of kufr, and neither ta'wil nor taqlid excuses one from the charge of kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about God or religion without scrutinizing it, simply because you were raised that way? If that belief were actually a form of kufr, would you want to know? What steps will you take today to examine your core beliefs with 'adna nazar' (minimal reflection)?
?
If someone you love—a family member or close friend—holds a belief that falls into one of these four types of kufr, do you have the courage to lovingly correct them, or do you stay silent out of comfort? What does your answer reveal about your own fear of truth or your attachment to them over God?
?
This lesson states that even minimal reflection would expose the error of clear kufr. Is there any area of your faith where you have been content with lazy certainty—assuming you are right without ever really checking? Will you let that complacency stand until the Day when no excuse will avail?

Hidden Kufr: Statements with Unintended Implications
Sanusi defines hidden kufr and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of statements that indirectly imply kufr and the specific examples Sanusi provides.

Core Idea
Some theological errors secretly imply kufr without the speaker realizing.

Sanusi begins by identifying a specific category of theological statements: those that carry a hidden implication of deficiency or disbelief. He lists several examples drawn from theological debates of his time, showing how speculative positions can inadvertently lead to kufr. This lesson lays out the category and its examples so you can see the range of issues involved.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the passage carefully (up to 'الْمُفْضِي إِلَى الْهَوَى وَالْبِدْعَةِ'). Notice how Sanusi defines the category before listing examples.
The passage uses 'لُزُومًا خَفِيًّا' to highlight the hidden nature of the implication.
2
Identify the category
The category is those who say a statement that necessarily (luzum) implies deficiency or kufr, but in a hidden way that the speaker does not perceive.
This distinguishes it from open kufr.
3
Review the examples
Sanusi gives several examples: asserting direction for Allah, denying the eternal attributes while affirming modal attributes, attributing independent power to creatures, affirming resemblance or a limb, and negating an attribute of perfection via erroneous interpretation.
Each example is a theological position that indirectly entails kufr.
4
Reflect on the hidden nature
Consider why the speaker might not realize the implication. This often arises from ijtihad or following a school without full awareness of consequences.
This sets up the later disagreement on takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّمَا اخْتَلَفُوا فِيمَنْ قَالَ قَوْلًا يَلْزَمُ عَنْهُ النَّقْصُ أَوِ الْكُفْرُ لُزُومًا خَفِيًّا لَمْ يَشْعُرْ بِهِ قَائِلُهُ، كَالْقَوْلِ بِالْجِهَةِ فِي حَقِّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَإِنْكَارِ صِفَاتِ الْمَعَانِي دُونَ الْمَعْنَوِيَّةِ، وَإِضَافَةِ الْأَفْعَالِ الِاخْتِيَارِيَّةِ إِلَى قُدَرِ الْحَيَوَانَاتِ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الِاسْتِقْلَالِ، وَإِثْبَاتِ تَشْبِيهٍ أَوْ نَعْتٍ بِجَارِحَةٍ، أَوْ نَفْيِ صِفَةِ كَمَالٍ عَلَى طَرِيقِ التَّأْوِيلِ وَالِاجْتِهَادِ الْمُخْطِئِ الْمُفْضِي إِلَى الْهَوَى وَالْبِدْعَةِ، فَهَذَا النَّوْعُ مِمَّا اخْتَلَفَ السَّلَفُ وَالْخَلَفُ فِي تَكْفِيرِ قَائِلِهِ وَمُعْتَقِدِهِ. فَقَالَ الْقَاضِي عِيَاضٌ: (وَأَكْثَرُ أَقْوَالِ السَّلَفِ تَكْفِيرُهُمْ) ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ: أَنَّ مِنَ الْفُقَهَاءِ وَالْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ مَنْ صَوَّبَ التَّكْفِيرَ الَّذِي قَالَ بِهِ الْجُمْهُورُ مِنَ السَّلَفِ، وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ أَبَاهُ وَلَمْ يَرَ إِخْرَاجَهُمْ مِنْ سَوَادِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَكْثَرِ الْفُقَهَاءِ وَالْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ.
And they only disagreed concerning one who said a statement from which necessarily follows deficiency or disbelief in a hidden way of which the speaker is not aware, like the statement of direction with respect to Allah Almighty, and denying the attributes of meanings while affirming the modal attributes, and attributing voluntary actions to the powers of animals as independent, and affirming resemblance or a description with a limb, or negating an attribute of perfection by way of misinterpretation and erroneous ijtihad leading to desire and innovation. So this type is among what the Salaf and Khalaf disagreed about regarding takfir of its speaker and believer. And Qadi Iyad said: 'Most statements of the Salaf declare them disbelievers.' Then he mentioned: that among the jurists and theologians are those who affirmed the takfir which the majority of the Salaf held, and among them are those who refused it and did not consider removing them from the flock of believers, and this is the saying of most jurists and theologians.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage discusses the disagreement among scholars regarding takfir (excommunication) of those who hold theological positions that indirectly imply kufr or deficiency about Allah, without the person realizing the implication. The author gives examples: asserting direction for Allah, denying the eternal attributes while affirming modal attributes, attributing independent power to creatures, affirming anthropomorphism, or negating an attribute of perfection through mistaken interpretation. The Salaf (early generations) and Khalaf (later) differed: Qadi Iyad reported that most Salaf sayings lean toward takfir. However, many jurists and theologians (including later ones) refrained from takfir and kept such persons within the community. The author concludes by noting that the position of not excommunicating is the view of most jurists and theologians. This shows a nuanced approach: while the error is serious, the visibility of the implication matters, and extreme caution is exercised in applying takfir.

Key Terms
لزوم
الجهة
صفات المعاني
قدر الحيوانات
تشبيه
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every theological error automatically makes one a disbeliever.
Correction: Sanusi shows that only statements with a hidden implication of kufr are in dispute; the speaker may be unaware, so excommunication is not automatic.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what characterizes the statements under dispute?
A) They are clearly kufr statements uttered intentionally
B) They are statements that necessarily imply deficiency or kufr in a hidden way
C) They are statements made by non-Muslims
D) They are statements that only the Salaf made

Key Takeaway
Statements that secretly imply kufr form a distinct category where the speaker's unawareness complicates the ruling on takfir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever made a statement about Allah without fully considering its theological implications? What would it take for you to examine your own speech for hidden kufr, even if you never intended it?
?
Sanusi lists denying attributes of meanings while affirming modal attributes as a form of hidden kufr. Do you hold any belief about Allah's attributes that you have not thought through to its logical end? Are you willing to have that belief tested against the criteria of this lesson?
?
The speaker in hidden kufr is unaware of the implication. Could you be unwittingly holding a position that logically leads to kufr, simply because you followed a scholar or a common teaching without verifying its foundations? What would it cost you to investigate?

The Disagreement on Takfir for Hidden Kufr
Sanusi reports the scholarly disagreement on takfir and the majority view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement among scholars regarding takfir for those who hold statements that secretly imply kufr, including the positions of the Salaf and later jurists and theologians.

Core Idea
Most Salaf declared takfir, but later scholars refrained from excommunication.

After defining the category of hidden kufr, Sanusi turns to the rulings. He reports Qadi Iyad's observation that most Salaf held takfir for such individuals. However, he then notes that many jurists and theologians did not remove them from the community. This lesson surveys the two positions and explains the reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'فَهَذَا النَّوْعُ' to the end. Notice how Sanusi cites Qadi Iyad and then summarizes the two views.
The passage uses 'اخْتَلَفَ' to signal disagreement.
2
Understand Qadi Iyad's report
Qadi Iyad stated that most statements of the Salaf declare such individuals disbelievers. This shows the weight of the early community's stance.
The Salaf were known for strictness on tawhid.
3
Identify the two positions
Some jurists and theologians affirmed the takfir held by the Salaf majority; others refused it and kept them within the fold of believers.
The second position is attributed to 'most jurists and theologians'.
4
Note the majority later view
Sanusi concludes that the view of not excommunicating is the saying of most jurists and theologians. This indicates a preference for caution.
This does not mean the error is condoned, only that takfir is avoided.

Then he mentioned: that among the jurists and theologians are those who affirmed the takfir which the majority of the Salaf held, and among them are those who refused it and did not consider removing them from the flock of believers, and this is the saying of most jurists and theologians.

?

?
The Salaf are often seen as the pinnacle of understanding. If most of them declared takfir, yet later scholars refrained, how do you reconcile your respect for the Salaf with the later scholars' caution? Are you willing to follow the later majority, or do you feel a need to side with the Salaf even on this issue?
?
Imagine you are in a position of authority and someone is accused of hidden kufr. Would you dare to excommunicate them based on your own understanding, or would you defer to the cautious approach of the majority of scholars? What is at stake for you personally in that decision?

Defining Implicit Kufr in Kalam
Sanusi defines implicit kufr and lists examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what constitutes a statement that implicitly implies kufr without the speaker's awareness, and be able to identify examples given by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Some statements imply kufr hiddenly, even if the speaker is unaware.

Before discussing the scholarly disagreement on takfir, Sanusi first clarifies the type of statements under debate. These are not explicit declarations of disbelief, but statements that logically entail deficiency or kufr in a subtle way. Understanding this category is crucial for following the subsequent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice that Sanusi begins by stating the disagreement concerns a specific type of speaker.
The key phrase is 'لزوماً خفياً' (hidden implication).
2
Identify the examples
Sanusi gives five examples of statements that implicitly imply deficiency or kufr. List each one and reflect on why they are problematic.
These examples cover theological errors like anthropomorphism and denial of divine attributes.
3
Reflect on the concept
Consider why the speaker's awareness matters. The passage emphasises that the speaker does not perceive the implication. How does this affect the ruling?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنَّما اختلفوا فيمَنْ قالَ قولاً يلزمُ عنهُ النقصُ أو الكفر لزوماً خفياً لم يشعُر بهِ قائله كالقول بالجهة في حقٌّ الله تعالى ، وإنكار صفاتِ المعاني دونَ المعنوية ، وإضافة الأفعال الاختياريَّةِ إِلى قُدَرِ الحيوانات على سبيل الاستقلال ، وإثباتِ تشبيه أو نعت بجارحة ، أو نفي صفة كمال على طريق التأويل والاجتهادِ المخطئ المفضي إلى الهوى والبدعة، فهذا النوعُ ممَّا اختلف السلفُ والخلف في تكفير قائلهِ ومُعتقده. فقال القاضي عياض : ( وأكثر أقوال السلف تكفيرهم ) ثم ذكرَ : أَنَّ مِنَ الفقهاء والمتكلمينَ مَنْ صَوَّبَ التكفير الذي قالَ بِهِ الجمهورُ مِنَ السلفِ ، ومنهم مَنْ أباه ولم يرَ إخراجهم مِنْ سوادِ المؤمنين ، وهو قول أكثر الفقهاء والمتكلمين. وقال : ( هم فسَّاقٌ عصاةٌ ضُلال ، ونورتُهم مِنَ المسلمين ، ونحكم لهم بأحكامهم ، ولهذا قال سحنون : لا إعادة على مَنْ صَلَّى خلفهم ، قال : وهو قولُ أصحاب مالك ؛ منهم المغيرة وابنُ كنانة وأشهبُ ، قال : لأنه مسلم ، وذنبُهُ لم يخرجهُ مِنَ الإسلام . واضطرب آخرون في ذلكَ ، ووقفوا عن القول بالتكفير أو ضده ، واختلافُ قَوْلَيْ مالك في ذلكَ ، وتوقفه عن إعادة الصلاة خلفهم منه ) وإلى نحو هذا ذهب القاضي أبو بكر إمام أهل التحقيقِ والحق ، وقال : إنَّها مِنَ المُعْوِصاتِ ؛ إذ القومُ لم يُصرحوا بالكفر ، وإنما قالوا قولاً يُؤدي إليه . واضطربَ قوله في المسألة على نحو اضطراب إمامِهِ مالكِ بنِ أنس ، حتى قال في بعض كلامه : إنَّهم على رأْيِ مَنْ كَفَّرَهم بالتأويل لا تحلُّ مناكحتهم ولا أكل ذبائحهم ، ولا الصلاة على ميّتهم ويُختلفُ في مواريثهم على الخلاف في ميراث المرتد بتكفيرهم ، وترك قتلهم ، والمبالغة في عقوبتهم ، وإطالة سجنهم ؛ حتى يظهر إقلاعهم ، وتستبين توبتهم ؛ كما فعل عمر رضي الله عنه بصبيغ
They only disagreed concerning the one who says a statement that necessarily implies deficiency or disbelief in a hidden way, which its speaker does not perceive, such as saying that Allah has a direction, denying the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) while affirming the attributive (al-maʿnawiyya), ascribing voluntary acts independently to the powers of animals, affirming likeness or a description with a bodily organ, or negating an attribute of perfection by way of misinterpretation and erroneous ijtihād that leads to whim and innovation. This is the type concerning which the predecessors (salaf) and successors (khalaf) differed regarding declaring its speaker and adherent a disbeliever (takfīr). Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ said: “Most of the sayings of the salaf declare them disbelievers.” Then he mentioned that among the jurists and theologians (mutakallimūn) are those who affirmed the takfīr that the majority of the salaf held, and among them are those who rejected it and did not consider removing them from the body of believers, and this is the saying of most of the jurists and theologians. And he said: “They are wicked, disobedient, strayers; we inherit from them as Muslims, and we judge them according to their rulings. For this reason Saḥnūn said: ‘No repetition is required for one who prayed behind them.’ He said: this is the saying of the companions of Mālik—among them al-Mughīra, Ibn Kināna, and Ashhab. He said: because he is a Muslim, and his sin does not remove him from Islam. Others wavered in this matter and refrained from stating takfīr or its opposite. And Mālik’s two sayings differed on this, and his hesitation about repeating prayer behind them is part of this.” And Qāḍī Abū Bakr—the imam of the people of verification and truth—leaned toward this view and said: “This is among the difficult matters, because those people did not explicitly state disbelief, but only said a statement that leads to it.” And his saying on the issue wavered like the wavering of his imam Mālik ibn Anas, to the point that he said in some of his words: “If one holds the view of those who declare them disbelievers due to misinterpretation, then marriage to them is not lawful, nor eating their slaughtered meat, nor praying over their dead. And there is disagreement concerning their inheritance according to the disagreement over the inheritance of an apostate. But they are not killed, rather they are severely punished and imprisoned for a long time until their renunciation appears and their repentance becomes clear, as ʿUmar—may Allah be pleased with him—did with Ṣubaygh.”
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the disagreement among Muslim scholars (both the salaf and the khalaf) regarding the ruling of takfīr (declaring someone a disbeliever) when a person makes a statement that implicitly implies deficiency or disbelief, but the speaker himself does not realize it. The author, Sanusi, first defines the nature of such statements: they are statements that necessarily entail (luzūman khafiyyan) either a deficiency or disbelief, but the speaker is unaware of the implication. Examples include: saying Allah has a direction (jiha), denying the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) while still affirming the attributive attributes (al-sifāt al-maʿnawiyya), ascribing voluntary acts independently to the powers of animals (i.e., denying that all actions are created by Allah), affirming likeness or describing Allah with a bodily organ (jāriḥa), or negating an attribute of perfection based on misinterpretation (taʾwīl) and mistaken ijtihād that leads to whim and innovation. Sanusi then states that this type of statement is the subject of disagreement between the salaf (early generations) and the khalaf (later generations) concerning whether its speaker should be declared a disbeliever. He then cites Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ, who said that most of the sayings of the salaf declare such people disbelievers. However, Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ also mentioned that among the jurists and theologians, there are two positions: one affirming the takfīr held by the salaf majority, and another rejecting takfīr and not removing such people from the community of believers—and this latter view is the position of most jurists and theologians. The author then presents a quote from an unnamed source (likely Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ continuing) describing those who err in these matters as wicked, disobedient, and straying, yet they are still treated as Muslims: they are inherited from, their prayers behind are valid (citing Saḥnūn), and they are not excommunicated. Mālik reportedly had two opinions on this, and some scholars wavered. Then Sanusi discusses the view of Qāḍī Abū Bakr (al-Bāqillānī), who considered the matter difficult because the people did not explicitly state kufr, only a statement that leads to it. Al-Bāqillānī's opinion wavered like that of his imam Mālik, and he even stated that if one follows the view of those who declare them disbelievers due to interpretation, then marriage and eating their meat are forbidden, and there is disagreement on inheritance. However, they are not killed but rather punished and imprisoned until repentance, as ʿUmar did with Ṣubaygh. The passage thus presents a nuanced view of takfīr: while some early scholars were strict, many later scholars (including the majority of jurists and theologians) refrained from excommunication, keeping them within the fold of Islam despite their errors.

Key Terms
جهة (jiha)
صفات المعاني (sifāt al-maʿānī)
تأويل (taʾwīl)
اجتهاد مخطئ (ijtihād mukhtiʾ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All statements that imply kufr automatically make the speaker a disbeliever.
Correction: Sanusi specifies that these are statements that imply kufr in a hidden way, and the speaker may be unaware; it is not explicit kufr.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the key characteristic of the statements under discussion?
A) They are explicit declarations of disbelief.
B) They necessarily imply deficiency or disbelief in a hidden way, and the speaker is unaware.
C) They are made only by non-Muslims.
D) They are all related to divine attributes.

Key Takeaway
Implicit kufr refers to statements that logically entail disbelief in a hidden manner, even if the speaker does not realize it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have I ever said something about Allah or His attributes without considering the full implications of my words? What might that reveal about my vigilance in speaking about the Divine?
?
This lesson shows that ignorance does not remove the implication of kufr from a statement. Am I actively seeking knowledge to ensure that my beliefs and words align with the correct understanding of Allah?
?
If I were to be held accountable for an implicit kufr I uttered unknowingly, would I be prepared to repent and correct it? What steps can I take today to purify my creed from hidden errors?

Scholarly Disagreement on Takfir of Implicit Kufr
Sanusi reports scholarly disagreement on takfir for implicit kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the range of scholarly opinions—from the salaf to later scholars—on whether to declare a disbeliever one who makes a statement that implicitly implies kufr.

Core Idea
Scholars disagreed: some declared takfir, others kept them within Islam.

After defining the type of statements, Sanusi turns to the central issue: should the speaker be declared a disbeliever (takfir)? He reports the views of the early generations (salaf) and later scholars (khalaf), highlighting that many jurists and theologians refrained from excommunication. He also discusses the nuanced stance of Qāḍī Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī and the precedent of Caliph ʿUmar with Ṣubaygh.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Sanusi first states the topic of disagreement, then quotes Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ and Qāḍī Abū Bakr.
Look for the phrase 'اختلف السلف والخلف'.
2
Identify the two main positions
According to Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ, what are the positions among jurists? One affirms takfir, the other rejects it. Which is the majority view?
The majority view is to not remove them from the body of believers.
3
Consider al-Bāqillānī's view
Qāḍī Abū Bakr considered the matter difficult. He gave different rulings depending on which position one follows. What practical implications does he mention?
He mentions marriage, food, prayer, inheritance, and punishment.
4
Reflect on the example of ʿUmar
Sanusi ends with the story of ʿUmar and Ṣubaygh. How does this illustrate the approach of punishment without excommunication?
