⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنَّما اختلفوا فيمَنْ قالَ قولاً يلزمُ عنهُ النقصُ أو الكفر لزوماً خفياً لم يشعُر بهِ قائله كالقول بالجهة في حقٌّ الله تعالى ، وإنكار صفاتِ المعاني دونَ المعنوية ، وإضافة الأفعال الاختياريَّةِ إِلى قُدَرِ الحيوانات على سبيل الاستقلال ، وإثباتِ تشبيه أو نعت بجارحة ، أو نفي صفة كمال على طريق التأويل والاجتهادِ المخطئ المفضي إلى الهوى والبدعة، فهذا النوعُ ممَّا اختلف السلفُ والخلف في تكفير قائلهِ ومُعتقده. فقال القاضي عياض : ( وأكثر أقوال السلف تكفيرهم ) ثم ذكرَ : أَنَّ مِنَ الفقهاء والمتكلمينَ مَنْ صَوَّبَ التكفير الذي قالَ بِهِ الجمهورُ مِنَ السلفِ ، ومنهم مَنْ أباه ولم يرَ إخراجهم مِنْ سوادِ المؤمنين ، وهو قول أكثر الفقهاء والمتكلمين. وقال : ( هم فسَّاقٌ عصاةٌ ضُلال ، ونورتُهم مِنَ المسلمين ، ونحكم لهم بأحكامهم ، ولهذا قال سحنون : لا إعادة على مَنْ صَلَّى خلفهم ، قال : وهو قولُ أصحاب مالك ؛ منهم المغيرة وابنُ كنانة وأشهبُ ، قال : لأنه مسلم ، وذنبُهُ لم يخرجهُ مِنَ الإسلام . واضطرب آخرون في ذلكَ ، ووقفوا عن القول بالتكفير أو ضده ، واختلافُ قَوْلَيْ مالك في ذلكَ ، وتوقفه عن إعادة الصلاة خلفهم منه ) وإلى نحو هذا ذهب القاضي أبو بكر إمام أهل التحقيقِ والحق ، وقال : إنَّها مِنَ المُعْوِصاتِ ؛ إذ القومُ لم يُصرحوا بالكفر ، وإنما قالوا قولاً يُؤدي إليه . واضطربَ قوله في المسألة على نحو اضطراب إمامِهِ مالكِ بنِ أنس ، حتى قال في بعض كلامه : إنَّهم على رأْيِ مَنْ كَفَّرَهم بالتأويل لا تحلُّ مناكحتهم ولا أكل ذبائحهم ، ولا الصلاة على ميّتهم ويُختلفُ في مواريثهم على الخلاف في ميراث المرتد بتكفيرهم ، وترك قتلهم ، والمبالغة في عقوبتهم ، وإطالة سجنهم ؛ حتى يظهر إقلاعهم ، وتستبين توبتهم ؛ كما فعل عمر رضي الله عنه بصبيغ
They only disagreed concerning the one who says a statement that necessarily implies deficiency or disbelief in a hidden way, which its speaker does not perceive, such as saying that Allah has a direction, denying the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) while affirming the attributive (al-maʿnawiyya), ascribing voluntary acts independently to the powers of animals, affirming likeness or a description with a bodily organ, or negating an attribute of perfection by way of misinterpretation and erroneous ijtihād that leads to whim and innovation. This is the type concerning which the predecessors (salaf) and successors (khalaf) differed regarding declaring its speaker and adherent a disbeliever (takfīr). Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ said: “Most of the sayings of the salaf declare them disbelievers.” Then he mentioned that among the jurists and theologians (mutakallimūn) are those who affirmed the takfīr that the majority of the salaf held, and among them are those who rejected it and did not consider removing them from the body of believers, and this is the saying of most of the jurists and theologians. And he said: “They are wicked, disobedient, strayers; we inherit from them as Muslims, and we judge them according to their rulings. For this reason Saḥnūn said: ‘No repetition is required for one who prayed behind them.’ He said: this is the saying of the companions of Mālik—among them al-Mughīra, Ibn Kināna, and Ashhab. He said: because he is a Muslim, and his sin does not remove him from Islam. Others wavered in this matter and refrained from stating takfīr or its opposite. And Mālik’s two sayings differed on this, and his hesitation about repeating prayer behind them is part of this.” And Qāḍī Abū Bakr—the imam of the people of verification and truth—leaned toward this view and said: “This is among the difficult matters, because those people did not explicitly state disbelief, but only said a statement that leads to it.” And his saying on the issue wavered like the wavering of his imam Mālik ibn Anas, to the point that he said in some of his words: “If one holds the view of those who declare them disbelievers due to misinterpretation, then marriage to them is not lawful, nor eating their slaughtered meat, nor praying over their dead. And there is disagreement concerning their inheritance according to the disagreement over the inheritance of an apostate. But they are not killed, rather they are severely punished and imprisoned for a long time until their renunciation appears and their repentance becomes clear, as ʿUmar—may Allah be pleased with him—did with Ṣubaygh.”
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the disagreement among Muslim scholars (both the salaf and the khalaf) regarding the ruling of takfīr (declaring someone a disbeliever) when a person makes a statement that implicitly implies deficiency or disbelief, but the speaker himself does not realize it. The author, Sanusi, first defines the nature of such statements: they are statements that necessarily entail (luzūman khafiyyan) either a deficiency or disbelief, but the speaker is unaware of the implication. Examples include: saying Allah has a direction (jiha), denying the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-maʿānī) while still affirming the attributive attributes (al-sifāt al-maʿnawiyya), ascribing voluntary acts independently to the powers of animals (i.e., denying that all actions are created by Allah), affirming likeness or describing Allah with a bodily organ (jāriḥa), or negating an attribute of perfection based on misinterpretation (taʾwīl) and mistaken ijtihād that leads to whim and innovation. Sanusi then states that this type of statement is the subject of disagreement between the salaf (early generations) and the khalaf (later generations) concerning whether its speaker should be declared a disbeliever. He then cites Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ, who said that most of the sayings of the salaf declare such people disbelievers. However, Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ also mentioned that among the jurists and theologians, there are two positions: one affirming the takfīr held by the salaf majority, and another rejecting takfīr and not removing such people from the community of believers—and this latter view is the position of most jurists and theologians. The author then presents a quote from an unnamed source (likely Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ continuing) describing those who err in these matters as wicked, disobedient, and straying, yet they are still treated as Muslims: they are inherited from, their prayers behind are valid (citing Saḥnūn), and they are not excommunicated. Mālik reportedly had two opinions on this, and some scholars wavered. Then Sanusi discusses the view of Qāḍī Abū Bakr (al-Bāqillānī), who considered the matter difficult because the people did not explicitly state kufr, only a statement that leads to it. Al-Bāqillānī's opinion wavered like that of his imam Mālik, and he even stated that if one follows the view of those who declare them disbelievers due to interpretation, then marriage and eating their meat are forbidden, and there is disagreement on inheritance. However, they are not killed but rather punished and imprisoned until repentance, as ʿUmar did with Ṣubaygh. The passage thus presents a nuanced view of takfīr: while some early scholars were strict, many later scholars (including the majority of jurists and theologians) refrained from excommunication, keeping them within the fold of Islam despite their errors.

Key Terms
تكفير (takfīr)
سلف (salaf)
خلف (khalaf)
قاضي عياض (Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ)
قاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني (Qāḍī Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All scholars agree on takfir for those who make statements implying disbelief.
Correction: The passage shows significant disagreement, with most later jurists and theologians refraining from takfir.

Checkpoint
According to Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ, what is the view of most jurists and theologians regarding those who make statements that implicitly lead to kufr?
A) They should be declared disbelievers without exception.
B) They are not to be removed from the body of believers and are treated as Muslims.
C) They are to be killed immediately.
D) They are to be imprisoned for life without possibility of repentance.

Key Takeaway
Despite the strictness of some early scholars, the majority of later jurists and theologians did not excommunicate those who made statements implicitly implying kufr, treating them as Muslims in legal matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone whose belief you consider misguided, do you rush to judge them as outside Islam, or do you follow the caution of the scholars in this lesson? What does your heart tell you about your own tendency toward takfir?
?
The scholars in this passage still treated those with faulty beliefs as Muslims in legal matters like marriage and inheritance. Is there a person in your life whose belief you doubt, yet you still maintain family ties? How does this passage challenge you to reconsider your attitude?
?
Al-Bāqillānī said the matter is difficult because the people did not explicitly state disbelief. Have you ever accused someone of kufr based on an implication? How would this lesson change your approach?

Scholarly Caution on Takfir of Ahl al-Ta'wil
Survey of scholarly caution on takfir for erroneous interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the varied scholarly positions on whether to pronounce takfir on Muslims who err in interpretation (ahl al-ta'wil) and the overriding principle of caution.

Core Idea
Even the great scholars hesitated before pronouncing takfir on fellow Muslims.

This passage presents a survey of early Maliki, Ash'ari, and later scholarly opinions on the sensitive issue of takfir (excommunication) of those who fall into erroneous theological interpretations. You will see how leading imams like Malik, al-Baqillani, al-Ash'ari, and al-Juwayni exercised extreme caution, often refraining from outright takfir and emphasizing the grave consequences of expelling a Muslim from the faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic carefully and its translation. Notice the variety of scholars quoted.
The passage weaves together multiple statements.
2
Identify the initial position
Find the view attributed to Sahnun and Malik's companions. What do they say about praying behind such people?
They deem them sinful but still treat them as Muslims.
3
Analyze the fluctuation in later scholars
Al-Baqillani and al-Ash'ari both had fluctuating statements. Compare their views and note the consequences al-Baqillani outlines if takfir is applied.
Pay attention to the detailed consequences: marriage, inheritance, etc.
4
Understand the concluding principle
What is the final verdict given at the end? Why is takfir considered dangerous?
The passage ends with a strong warning against shedding Muslim blood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال : ( هم فسَّاقٌ عصاةٌ ضُلال ، ونورتُهم مِنَ المسلمين ، ونحكم لهم بأحكامهم ، ولهذا قال سحنون : لا إعادة على مَنْ صَلَّى خلفهم ، قال : وهو قولُ أصحاب مالك ؛ منهم المغيرة وابن كنانة وأشهبُ ، قال : لأنه مسلم ، وذنبُهُ لم يخرجهُ مِنَ الإسلام . واضطرب آخرون في ذلكَ ، ووقفوا عن القول بالتكفير أو ضده ، واختلافُ قَوْلَيْ مالك في ذلكَ ، وتوقفه عن إعادة الصلاة خلفهم .. وإلى نحو هذا ذهب القاضي أبو بكر إمام أهل التحقيقِ والحق ، وقال : إنَّها مِنَ المُعْوِصاتِ ؛ إذ القومُ لم يُصرحوا بالكفر ، وإنما قالوا قولاً يُؤدي إليه . واضطربَ قوله في المسألة على نحو اضطراب إمامِهِ مالكِ بنِ أنس ، حتى قال في بعض كلامه : إنَّهم على رأْيِ مَنْ كَفَّرَهم بالتأويل لا تحلُّ مناكحتهم ولا أكل ذبائحهم ، ولا الصلاة على ميّتهم ويُختلفُ في مواريثهم على الخلاف في ميراث المرتد بتكفيرهم ، وترك قتلهم ، والمبالغة في عقوبتهم ، وإطالة سجنهم ؛ حتى يظهر إقلاعهم ، وتستبين توبتهم ؛ كما فعل عمر رضي الله عنه بصبيغ . وقال أيضاً : نُورِّثُ ميْتَهم ورثتهم مِنَ المسلمينَ ، ولا نُورِّتُهم هم مِنَ المسلمين . وأكثر ميله إلى ترك التكفير بالمالِ . وكذلك اضطربَ فيهِ قولُ شيخِهِ الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري وأكثرُ قولِهِ تركُ التكفير ، وأنَّ الكفر خصلةٌ واحدةٌ ؛ وهو الجهلُ بوجود الباري تعالى . وقالَ مرَّةً : مَنِ اعتقد أنَّ الله تعالى جسم ، أو المسيح ، أو بعضُ مَنْ يلقاه في الطريقِ .. فليس بعارفِ بهِ ، وهو كافر . وإلى مثل هذا ذهب أبو المعالي رحمهُ اللهُ تعالى في أجوبتِهِ لأبي محمد عبد الحقِّ ، وكان سأله عن المسألة ، واعتذرَ لهُ بأنَّ الغلط فيها يصعبُ ؛ لأنَّ إدخال الكافر في الملَّةِ وإخراج المسلم منها .. أمرٌ عظيم في الدين . وقالَ غيرُهما مِنَ المحققين : الذي يجب الاحتراز منه التكفير في أهل التأويل ؛ فإنَّ استباحة دماء المسلمين الموحدينَ خَطَرٌ .
And he said: (They are immoral, disobedient, misguided. We place them among the Muslims and judge them by their judgments. For this reason Sahnun said: No repetition is required for one who prayed behind them. He said: This is the statement of Malik's companions; among them al-Mughira, Ibn Kināna, and Ashhab. He said: Because he is a Muslim, and his sin did not remove him from Islam.) Others differed concerning that and hesitated to pronounce takfir or its opposite. And there is disagreement between the two statements of Malik concerning that, and his hesitation about repeating prayer behind them. The Qāḍī Abū Bakr, the imam of the people of verification and truth, inclined toward this and said: It is among the difficult issues, since the people did not explicitly state unbelief, but rather they said a statement that leads to it. And his statement fluctuated on the matter similar to the fluctuation of his imam Mālik ibn Anas, until he said in some of his speech: According to the opinion of those who declare them unbelievers due to interpretation, neither is marriage with them permissible nor eating their slaughtered animals, nor praying over their dead. And their inheritance is differed over according to the disagreement on the inheritance of an apostate due to their takfir. And they are not to be killed, but their punishment is to be intensified and their imprisonment prolonged until their renunciation appears and their repentance becomes clear, as ʿUmar, may Allah be pleased with him, did with Ṣabīgh. And he also said: We give inheritance from their deceased to their heirs from the Muslims, and we do not give inheritance to them from the Muslims. And his inclination was mostly toward refraining from takfir because of [this] property. Likewise the statement of his shaykh, Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī, fluctuated concerning it, and most of his statement was refraining from takfir, and that unbelief is a single trait, which is ignorance of the existence of the Exalted Creator. And he said once: Whoever believes that Allah, exalted, is a body, or the Messiah, or someone he meets in the street, is not knowledgeable of Him and is an unbeliever. Abū al-Maʿālī, may Allah have mercy on him, went to something similar in his responses to Abū Muḥammad ʿAbd al-Ḥaqq, who had asked him about the matter. And he apologized to him because the error in it is difficult, since including an unbeliever in the religion and expelling a Muslim from it is a grave matter in religion. And others among the verifiers said: What must be avoided is takfir of those who practice interpretation (ahl al-taʾwīl), for permitting the blood of monotheist Muslims is a danger.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a survey of scholarly positions on whether to declare takfir (excommunication) upon Muslims who hold erroneous beliefs due to interpretive mistakes (taʾwīl). It begins by quoting a statement describing such people as sinful but still judged as Muslims, citing Sahnun's view that prayer behind them is valid, and that this is the position of Malik's companions. Others hesitated and Malik himself had two statements. The Qadi Abu Bakr (al-Baqillani) considered it a difficult issue since they did not explicitly disbelieve but said something leading to it; his view fluctuated like Malik's, and he detailed consequences if they are considered unbelievers by interpretation: no marriage, no eating their slaughtered meat, no prayer over their dead, and inheritance treated like apostasy, but not killed; instead, punishment and imprisonment until repentance, like 'Umar did with Sabigh. Al-Baqillani also said that their Muslim heirs inherit from them, but they do not inherit from Muslims. Mostly he inclined to avoid takfir. Then al-Ash'ari's view is presented: mostly refraining from takfir, defining unbelief as ignorance of God's existence, but he once said that whoever believes God is a body or the Messiah or a random person is an unbeliever. Then al-Juwayni (Abu al-Ma'ali) in his responses emphasized the gravity of the error, as admitting an unbeliever into the faith or expelling a Muslim is serious. Finally, the passage concludes with the principle that takfir of ahl al-ta'wil must be avoided, since shedding the blood of monotheist Muslims is dangerous.

Key Terms
takfir
ahl al-ta'wil
fasiq
al-Baqillani
al-Ash'ari
al-Juwayni
Sahnun
Malik

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All early scholars agreed on immediate takfir of those with theological errors.
Correction: In fact, many great scholars like Malik, al-Baqillani, al-Ash'ari, and al-Juwayni hesitated or avoided takfir, emphasizing caution.

Checkpoint
What is the overall conclusion of the passage regarding takfir of ahl al-ta'wil?
A) They should be declared unbelievers immediately.
B) Takfir should be avoided because it risks shedding the blood of Muslims.
C) Only al-Ash'ari opposed takfir.
D) The issue is simple and clear.

Key Takeaway
The consensus of the scholars surveyed is to exercise extreme caution and generally avoid takfir of those who err in interpretation, as the risk of wrongly shedding Muslim blood is great.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a fellow Muslim with a theological mistake, does your heart race to correct them or to cover them? Which response does the caution of these scholars demand of you today?
?
You carry the power to label someone's faith as valid or invalid. How have you used that power in the past week? Will you now stand before Allah with that record?
?
The scholars did not rush to takfir, even for major errors. What would it take for you to suspend your judgment and hope for someone's repentance, as they did?

Scholarly Positions on Takfir of Ahl al-Ta’wil
The author reports positions of al-Baqillani, al-Ash'ari, and al-Juwayni on takfir, and the principle of caution from the investigators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the varying positions of leading Ash'ari scholars on the issue of takfir of theological innovators and the overriding principle of caution.

Core Idea
Takfir is a grave matter; the scholars leaned toward caution and refraining.

This lesson examines the cautious approach of major Sunni theologians toward declaring theological innovators (ahl al-ta’wil) disbelievers. We will see how al-Baqillani, al-Ash'ari, and al-Juwayni all expressed hesitation, and how the later investigators elevated the principle that sparing a thousand non-believers is better than shedding a single Muslim's blood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the flow of different opinions.
Notice the use of footnotes (1), (2), (4) which are editorial clarifications.
2
Identify each scholar's position
List the positions of al-Baqillani, al-Ash'ari, and al-Juwayni. Note any contradictions or shifts in their statements.
Al-Ash'ari is reported to have two different opinions.
3
Analyze the principle of the investigators
Focus on the statement about leaving a thousand disbelievers being lighter than shedding one Muslim's blood. Why is this principle so powerful?
This reflects the high sanctity of Muslim life.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how these scholars prioritized caution over hasty excommunication.

وقال أيضاً : نُورِّثُ ميْتَهم ورثتهم مِنَ المسلمينَ ، ولا نُورِّتُهم هم مِنَ المسلمين . وأكثر ميله (۱) إلى ترك التكفير بالمالِ وكذلك اضطربَ فيهِ قولُ شيخِهِ الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري وأكثرُ قولِهِ تركُ التكفير ، وأنَّ الكفر خصلةٌ واحدةٌ ؛ وهو الجهلُ بوجود الباري تعالى . وقالَ مرَّةً : مَنِ اعتقد أنَّ الله تعالى جسم ، أو المسيح ، أو بعضُ مَنْ يلقاه في الطريقِ .. فليس بعارفِ بهِ ، وهو كافر . وإلى مثل هذا (۲) : ذهب أبو المعالي رحمهُ اللهُ تعالى في أجوبتِهِ لأبي محمد عبد الحقِّ ، وكان سأله عن المسألة ، واعتذرَ لهُ بأنَّ الغلط فيها يصعبُ ؛ لأنَّ إدخال الكافر في الملَّةِ وإخراج المسلم منها .. أمرٌ عظيم في الدين . وقالَ غيرُهما مِنَ المحققين (٤) : الذي يجب الاحتراز منه التكفير في أهل التأويل ؛ فإنَّ استباحة دماء المسلمين الموحدينَ خَطَرٌ ، والخطاً في تركِ ألفِ كافرٍ أهونُ مِنَ الخطأ في سفكِ مِحْجَمَةٍ مِنْ دم مسلم واحد . وقد قالَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : « فَإِذَا قَالُوهَا » يعني : الشهادةَ عَصَمُوا مِنِّي دِمَاءَهُمْ وَأَمْوَالَهُمْ إِلا بِحَقِّهَا ، وَحِسَابُهُمْ عَلَى اللَّهِ »(۱) والعصمة مقطوع بها مع الشهادة ، ولا ترتفع ولا يُستباح خلافُها إلا بقاطع ، ولا قاطعَ مِنْ شرع ، ولا قياس عليه ، وألفاظ الأحاديثِ الواردة في البابِ مُعرَّضة للتأويل )(۲) ثم قال القاضي بعد هذا : ( والصواب : تركُ إكفارهم ، والإعراضُ عن الحتم عليهم بالخُسْرانِ ، وإجراء حكم الإسلام عليهم ؛ في قصاصهم، ووراثاتهم ، ومناكحاتهم ، ودياتهم ، والصلاة عليهم ، ودفنهم في مقابر المسلمين ، وسائر معاملاتهم ، لكنَّهم يُغَلَّظُ عليهم بوجيع الأدبِ وشديد الزجر والهجر ، حتى يرجعوا عن بدعتهم . وهذه كانَتْ سيرة الصدرِ الأَوَّلِ فيهم ، وقد كان نشأ على زمانِ الصحابة وبعدهم في التابعينَ مَنْ قالَ بهذه الأقوالِ ؛ مِنَ القدريَّةِ ورأي
He also said: We cause their dead to be inherited by their inheritors from the Muslims, and we do not cause them to inherit from the Muslims. And his leaning (1) is mostly toward refraining from declaring disbelief concerning property. And similarly the statement of his shaykh, Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari, was unsettled in this matter, and most of his statement is refraining from declaring disbelief, and that disbelief is one trait: ignorance of the existence of the Creator, exalted is He. And he said once: Whoever believes that Allah is a body, or al-Masih, or someone he meets on the road... then he is not a knower of Him, and he is a disbeliever. And to the like of this (2) went Abu al-Ma‘ali—may Allah have mercy on him—in his answers to Abu Muhammad ‘Abd al-Haqq, when he asked him about the issue, and he excused himself to him by saying that error in it is difficult, because admitting the disbeliever into the faith and expelling the Muslim from it... is a grave matter in religion. And others among the investigators (4) said: That which must be guarded against is declaring disbelief concerning the people of interpretation (ahl al-ta’wil); for making permissible the blood of Muslims who affirm the oneness of Allah is dangerous, and the error in leaving a thousand disbelievers is lighter than the error in shedding an ounce of the blood of a single Muslim. And the Prophet—peace and blessings be upon him—said: 'When they say it' meaning the shahada, 'they protect from me their blood and their wealth except by its right, and their reckoning is with Allah.' (1) And inviolability is definitively established with the shahada, and it is not lifted nor is its contravention made permissible except by a decisive proof, and there is no decisive proof from the Law, nor any analogy based on it, and the wordings of the hadiths reported in this chapter are subject to interpretation (2). Then al-Qadi said after this: The correct view is to refrain from declaring them disbelievers, and to avoid pronouncing upon them with loss, and to apply the rulings of Islam to them: in their retaliation, inheritances, marriages, blood-money, prayers over them, burial in Muslim cemeteries, and all their transactions. However, they are treated severely with painful discipline, strong rebuke, and ostracism, until they return from their innovation. And this was the practice of the early generation concerning them. And there had arisen in the time of the Companions and after them among the Followers those who said these statements, from the Qadariyya and the opinion...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage addresses the sensitive issue of takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever) specifically regarding ahl al-ta’wil (those who engage in interpretation, i.e., theological innovators). The author begins by reporting the stance of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani: he leans toward refraining from takfir in matters involving property (i.e., not declaring Muslims disbelievers due to financial sins). Then he notes that his teacher, al-Ash‘ari, had an unsettled position on this, but his predominant view is also refraining from takfir, defining disbelief as ignorance of the existence of God. Al-Ash‘ari is reported to have once said that anyone who believes God is a body, or al-Masih (a prophet), or even an ordinary person is not a true knower of God and is thereby a disbeliever—an apparent exception showing that extreme anthropomorphism might incur takfir. The author then mentions al-Juwayni (Abu al-Ma‘ali) who, in his answers to ‘Abd al-Haqq, agreed with a similar cautious approach, noting that error in this matter is serious because it involves either admitting a disbeliever into the faith or expelling a Muslim from it. Next, the author cites other investigators (al-muhaqqiqun) who emphasize that takfir must be avoided especially for ahl al-ta’wil, because it is dangerous to permit the blood of monotheistic Muslims. They make a powerful argument that leaving a thousand disbelievers un-killed is a lesser error than spilling even a small amount of a Muslim’s blood. This principle is then reinforced with a hadith of the Prophet, who said that when people utter the shahada (testimony of faith), their blood and property are protected except by due process (i.e., only with a clear legal justification), and their final judgment is with Allah. The author comments that this protection (isma) is definitively established with the shahada and cannot be removed or violated except by a decisive proof (qati‘), and there is no such proof from the Law or analogy that would justify takfir solely based on innovation—since many hadith wordings mentioning disbelief are subject to interpretation (e.g., referring to major sins but not actual apostasy). Then al-Qadi (al-Baqillani) gives the final ruling: the correct position is to refrain from declaring such people disbelievers, to avoid condemning them as losers, and to continue applying all Islamic rulings to them—retaliation, inheritance, marriage, blood-money, funeral prayer, burial, and all other transactions. However, they are to be severely disciplined, rebuked, and ostracized until they abandon their innovation. The author concludes that this was the consistent practice of the early Salaf, noting that even among the Companions and Followers there were those who held such views (from the Qadariyya, etc.), implying that despite their errors, they were not excommunicated.

Key Terms
takfir
ahl al-ta’wil
al-Ash‘ari
al-Baqillani
al-Juwayni

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That any theological innovation automatically makes a person a disbeliever whose blood is permissible.
Correction: The passage shows that the Salaf and leading scholars were extremely cautious and did not excommunicate innovators, only punishing them severely while still treating them as Muslims.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was al-Ash'ari's predominant view on takfir?
A) He declared all innovators disbelievers.
B) He refrained from declaring disbelief, defining disbelief as ignorance of God.
C) He had no opinion.
D) He only considered anthropomorphists as disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Leading Ash'ari scholars consistently warned against the grave error of takfir and prioritized preserving Muslim blood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been quick to judge a fellow Muslim who held a different opinion in matters where scholars differed? How does the caution of these imams challenge your attitude?
?
The investigators said error in sparing a thousand disbelievers is lighter than shedding one Muslim's blood. Are your internal judgments and words about other Muslims as careful as these scholars command?
?
When you hear someone labeled as a disbeliever, do you instantly accept it or do you recall the gravity of takfir as stated here? What practical step can you take to embody this caution?

The Hadith and Final Ruling on Takfir
The author cites the hadith on protection through shahada and presents al-Baqillani's final ruling that ahl al-ta’wil remain Muslims but are disciplined.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the legal basis for not excommunicating ahl al-ta’wil based on hadith and the final ruling of al-Qadi al-Baqillani.

Core Idea
The shahada guarantees inviolability; only a decisive proof can lift it.

This lesson focuses on the prophetic hadith about the protection of blood and wealth through the shahada, and al-Qadi al-Baqillani's conclusion that ahl al-ta’wil are still Muslims subject to Islamic law, though they may be disciplined.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its explanation
Read the hadith about the shahada granting protection. Note the comment about 'no decisive proof' for takfir.
The hadith is a key textual evidence from the Prophet.
2
Understand al-Qadi's ruling
Al-Qadi al-Baqillani enumerates the Islamic rulings that still apply to ahl al-ta’wil, and the disciplinary measures used against them.
Note the list of applied rulings: inheritance, marriage, burial, etc.
3
Connect to the early practice
The passage states that this was the practice of the early Salaf, and even among the Companions there were those who held innovated views but were not excommunicated.
This shows continuity of the cautious approach.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how the hadith and the ruling together establish a firm principle of not excommunicating unless there is decisive proof.

Commentary
This passage addresses the sensitive issue of takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever) specifically regarding ahl al-ta’wil (those who engage in interpretation, i.e., theological innovators). The author begins by reporting the stance of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani: he leans toward refraining from takfir in matters involving property (i.e., not declaring Muslims disbelievers due to financial sins). Then he notes that his teacher, al-Ash‘ari, had an unsettled position on this, but his predominant view is also refraining from takfir, defining disbelief as ignorance of the existence of God. Al-Ash‘ari is reported to have once said that anyone who believes God is a body, or al-Masih (a prophet), or even an ordinary person is not a true knower of God and is thereby a disbeliever—an apparent exception showing that extreme anthropomorphism might incur takfir. The author then mentions al-Juwayni (Abu al-Ma‘ali) who, in his answers to ‘Abd al-Haqq, agreed with a similar cautious approach, noting that error in this matter is serious because it involves either admitting a disbeliever into the faith or expelling a Muslim from it. Next, the author cites other investigators (al-muhaqqiqun) who emphasize that takfir must be avoided especially for ahl al-ta’wil, because it is dangerous to permit the blood of monotheistic Muslims. They make a powerful argument that leaving a thousand disbelievers un-killed is a lesser error than spilling even a small amount of a Muslim’s blood. This principle is then reinforced with a hadith of the Prophet, who said that when people utter the shahada (testimony of faith), their blood and property are protected except by due process (i.e., only with a clear legal justification), and their final judgment is with Allah. The author concludes that this was the consistent practice of the early Salaf, noting that even among the Companions and Followers there were those who held such views (from the Qadariyya, etc.), implying that despite their errors, they were not excommunicated.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith allows killing any innovator because their blood is no longer protected.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qadi al-Baqillani's ruling, what is the correct treatment of ahl al-ta’wil?
A) They are declared disbelievers and excommunicated.
B) They are not declared disbelievers but are treated as Muslims with severe discipline until they repent.
C) They are executed immediately.
D) They are ignored and left alone.

Key Takeaway
The final ruling is that ahl al-ta’wil are not excommunicated; they remain Muslims under Islamic law, though they are severely disciplined to return to the truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If the early Salaf dealt with innovators with discipline yet mercy, what would that look like in your own dealings with Muslims you disagree with? Will you commit to that balance, even when it is difficult?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
5 min
The Sanctity of Muslim Blood and the Hadith of Protection
Sanusi states the principle that sparing disbelievers is safer than shedding Muslim blood, citing a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that it is safer to err in sparing a thousand disbelievers than to err in shedding the blood of a single Muslim, and the implications of the hadith of protection for declaring someone a non-Muslim.

Core Idea
Protection (ʿiṣma) is definitively established by the shahada and cannot be removed without definitive proof.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a foundational principle regarding the sanctity of Muslim blood. He argues that the gravity of mistakenly harming a Muslim far outweighs that of sparing a disbeliever. He then supports this with a prophetic hadith that establishes the protection of life and wealth upon uttering the testimony of faith, clarifying the stringent conditions under which this protection may be lifted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: first a general principle, then a hadith, then the author's commentary. This will help you follow the logical flow.
The Arabic uses the word 'مِحْجَمَة' for a small amount of blood, emphasizing that even a tiny amount is significant.
2
Identify the main principle
Sanusi states: 'الخطأ في ترك ألف كافر أهون من الخطأ في سفك محجمة من دم مسلم واحد.' This sets a clear priority: errors of leniency towards non-Muslims are far less serious than errors that harm a Muslim.
This principle is the foundation for the discussion that follows.
3
Examine the hadith of protection
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When they say it (the shahada), they have protected from me their blood and their wealth except by its right, and their account is with Allah.' Note the exception 'except by its right' which allows for legal punishment in some cases.
The phrase 'their account is with Allah' reminds us that we judge by outward actions, leaving inner faith to Allah.
4
Understand 'Iṣma and Qāṭiʿ
Sanusi explains that the protection (ʿiṣma) is definitively established by the shahada. It cannot be removed or violated except by a definitive proof (qāṭiʿ). He then states there is no such proof from the Law or analogy that would permit violating it.
This highlights the extreme caution required before declaring someone a non-Muslim.
5
Consider the implications
Sanusi concludes that other aḥādīth on this topic are subject to interpretation and cannot override the clear protection established by the shahada. This reinforces the principle of restraint in takfīr.
Errors in declaring someone a non-Muslim are far more dangerous than errors in the opposite direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخطاً في تركِ ألفِ كافرٍ أهونُ مِنَ الخطأ في سفكِ مِحْجَمَةٍ مِنْ دم مسلم واحد . وقد قالَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : « فَإِذَا قَالُوهَا » يعني : الشهادةَ عَصَمُوا مِنِّي دِمَاءَهُمْ وَأَمْوَالَهُمْ إِلا بِحَقِّهَا ، وَحِسَابُهُمْ عَلَى اللَّهِ »(۱) والعصمة مقطوع بها مع الشهادة ، ولا ترتفع ولا يُستباح خلافُها إلا بقاطع ، ولا قاطعَ مِنْ شرع ، ولا قياس عليه ، وألفاظ الأحاديثِ الواردة في البابِ مُعرَّضة للتأويل )(۲)
And error in leaving a thousand disbelievers is lighter than error in shedding the blood of a single Muslim from a cupping glass. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'When they say it' – meaning the testimony – 'they have protected from me their blood and their wealth except by its right, and their account is with Allah.' And protection (al-ʿiṣma) is definitively established with the testimony, and it is not removed nor is its contrary permitted except by a definitive proof, and there is no definitive proof from the Law, nor can it be established by analogy, and the wordings of the aḥādīth reported on this topic are subject to interpretation.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents a principle of Islamic jurisprudence regarding the sanctity of Muslim blood. It begins by stating that erring on the side of sparing a thousand disbelievers is less grave than erring by shedding even a small amount of a Muslim's blood. This establishes a strong presumption in favor of protecting those who claim to be Muslim. It then cites the famous hadith: when a person testifies to the shahada (testimony of faith), their blood and wealth are protected from the Prophet's community except for a right that legally overrides that protection, and their inner state is left to Allah. The author explains that this protection (ʿiṣma) is definitively established by the testimony itself. It cannot be lifted or violated except by a definitive proof (qāṭiʿ), and there is no such proof from the revealed law or analogy that would allow violating it without clear evidence. The author also notes that the wordings of other aḥādīth on this topic (which might seem to permit declaring Muslims disbelievers for sins) are subject to interpretation and cannot override this clear principle. The overall message is that declaring someone a non-Muslim (takfīr) requires the utmost caution, and errors in that direction are far more dangerous than errors in the opposite direction.

Key Terms
عصمة
شهادة
قاطع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that saying the shahada protects a person absolutely without any exception, or that a person who commits a major sin can be declared a non-Muslim.
Correction: The hadith includes the exception 'except by its right' (illā bi-ḥaqqihā), which allows for legal punishments in certain cases. However, the protection can only be removed by a definitive proof (qāṭiʿ), and no such proof exists for declaring a Muslim who has uttered the shahada to be a disbeliever.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on the protection (ʿiṣma) of a Muslim's blood and wealth when they have testified to the shahada?
A) It is conditional and can be removed by mere suspicion.
B) It is definitively established and can only be removed by a definitive proof (qāṭiʿ).
C) It is automatically voided if the person commits a major sin.
D) It is left entirely to the ruler's discretion.

Key Takeaway
The sanctity of a Muslim's blood and wealth is definitively established by the shahada and cannot be violated without a clear and definitive proof from the Law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a Muslim committing a sin you find grave, do you feel a sense of judgment or a sense of their lasting protection? How does the hadith 'their account is with Allah' confront your own tendency to assume their fate? This week, whenever you hear about a Muslim's fault, will you remind yourself that you are not their judge and that their blood remains sacred?
?
The error of sparing a thousand disbelievers is lighter than shedding the blood of a single Muslim. Reflect: In your heart, are you more concerned about the reputation of Islam or about the inviolability of individual Muslims? If you had to choose between defending a Muslim who brings shame to the community or upholding their God-given protection, which would you prioritize? What one action can you take to embody this hadith's reverence for Muslim blood?
?
The passage insists that protection can only be removed by a definitive proof from the Law. Have you ever, even silently, stripped someone of their Islamic identity based on a personal standard or a loose interpretation? What would it mean for you to submit your judgments to this rule—requiring a clear text from the Law before ever calling into question a Muslim's faith? Will you repent from any instance where you violated this sacred limit and commit to guarding your tongue from takfir?

The Correct Approach to Innovators: Applying Islamic Law Without Takfir
Qadi 'Iyad outlines the correct ruling for dealing with religious innovators without declaring them kafir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the balanced approach of Ahl al-Sunna toward religious innovators: maintaining their Islamic legal status while actively disciplining them.

Core Idea
Innovators remain Muslims in law, but face severe discipline until they repent.

How should we treat fellow Muslims who hold innovated beliefs that fall short of outright disbelief? Qadi 'Iyad provides a clear ruling: refrain from declaring them unbelievers, apply full Islamic law to them in all worldly matters, but simultaneously discipline them severely. This passage demonstrates the nuanced methodology of Ahl al-Sunna in dealing with religious deviance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: the Qadi first states the correct view, then lists the areas where Islamic law applies, then mentions the disciplinary measures.
The passage is a single sentence with three main parts.
2
Identify the two key components
The ruling has two parts: what we do (apply Islamic law) and what we do not do (declare them kafir or condemn them). Also note the disciplinary measures.
This balance is crucial.
3
Understand the list of applications
Notice the specific areas where Islamic law is applied: retaliation, inheritance, marriage, blood-money, funeral prayer, burial, and all transactions. This shows full legal integration.
It covers civil, criminal, and ritual aspects.
4
Reflect on the discipline
The discipline includes painful punishment, intense rebuke, and social boycott. Why these? To bring them back from innovation while preserving their Islam.
This refutes the misconception that innovation is tolerated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال القاضي بعد هذا : ( والصواب : تركُ إكفارهم ، والإعراضُ عن الحتم عليهم بالخُسْرانِ ، وإجراء حكم الإسلام عليهم ؛ في قصاصهم، ووراثاتهم ، ومناكحاتهم ، ودياتهم ، والصلاة عليهم ، ودفنهم في مقابر المسلمين ، وسائر معاملاتهم ، لكنَّهم يُغَلَّظُ عليهم بوجيع الأدبِ وشديد الزجر والهجر ، حتى يرجعوا عن بدعتهم )
Then the Qadi said after this: 'And the correct [view] is: refraining from declaring them unbelievers, and turning away from passing judgment on them of perdition, and applying the ruling of Islam upon them – in their retaliation, inheritances, marriages, blood-money, prayer over them, burial in Muslim cemeteries, and all their transactions – but they are treated severely with painful discipline and intense rebuke and boycott, until they return from their innovation.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (ḥukm) from Qadi 'Iyad regarding how to treat people who hold innovated beliefs that do not amount to outright disbelief. He states that the correct approach is to refrain from declaring them kāfir (takfīr) and to avoid condemning them to eternal loss. Instead, the full Islamic legal ruling applies to them in all external matters: they are subject to qisas (retaliation), inherit from and are inherited from, can contract valid marriages, receive and pay diya (blood-money), funeral prayer is performed over them, they are buried in Muslim cemeteries, and all their transactions are valid under Islamic law. However, they are not simply left alone; they are to be disciplined severely with painful punishment, strong rebuke, and social boycott (hajr) until they abandon their innovation. This approach balances preserving their status as Muslims in outward legal matters while actively opposing and correcting their deviant beliefs.

Key Terms

حكم الإسلام
بدعة
هجر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if someone is not declared kafir, their innovation is tolerated.
Correction: The passage shows that innovators are severely disciplined, so innovation is not tolerated even if they remain Muslim in legal rulings.

Checkpoint

B) The rulings of Islam are applied to them in all transactions except inheritance.
C) The rulings of Islam are applied to them in all transactions, but they are disciplined severely.
D) They are to be boycotted completely and no Islamic ruling applies.

Key Takeaway
Qadi 'Iyad teaches that innovators remain Muslims in all legal matters but must be disciplined until they abandon their innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Which extreme does your heart incline to, and what would it take for you to follow the balanced path of Qadi 'Iyad?
?

?
Qadi 'Iyad says innovators are disciplined 'until they return from their innovation.' When was the last time you took any real action—whether advice, rebuke, or prayer—to help someone leave a false belief? If not, why has your silence been more comfortable than obedience to this teaching?

The Salaf’s Treatment of Innovators
Sanusi describes the historical practice of the Salaf with innovators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the early Muslim community (Salaf) dealt with followers of deviant sects, balancing legal status as Muslims with severe disciplinary measures.

Core Idea
The Salaf disciplined innovators without declaring them outside Islam.

Sanusi provides a historical precedent that clarifies the Islamic response to theological deviation. The early generations faced sects like the Qadariyya, Khawarij, and Mu'tazila, and their approach was neither total excommunication nor lenient acceptance. This passage shows how they maintained Islamic legal rulings while applying harsh physical and social penalties according to the severity of the error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the author's exact wording and flow.
Notice the key terms: فساق, كبيرة, بدعة, هجر.
2
Identify the three sects mentioned
Locate the names Qadariyya, Khawarij, and Mu'tazila. Understand the basic deviation of each: Qadariyya denied predestination, Khawarij rebelled and excommunicated sinners, Mu'tazila emphasized rationalism.
3
Contrast what the Salaf DID and DID NOT do
The passage lists two things they did NOT do: displace graves and cut inheritance. Then lists what they DID: boycott, beating, exile, killing. Reflect on the balance between maintaining Muslim identity and imposing discipline.
Why keep inheritance? Because they considered them Muslims in legal rulings.
4
Understand the rationale
They were sinful but not kafir according to Ahl al-Sunna. The passage contrasts with those who held stricter views (declaring them kafir). This shows the mainstream position Sanusi advocates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه كانَتْ سيرة الصدرِ الأَوَّلِ فيهم ، وقد كان نشأ على زمانِ الصحابة وبعدهم في التابعينَ مَنْ قالَ بهذه الأقوالِ ؛ مِنَ القدريَّةِ ورأي الخوارج والاعتزال، فما أزاحوا لهم قبراً ، ولا قطعوا لأحدٍ منهم ميراثاً ، لكنهم هجروهم ، وأبوهم بالضرب والنفي والقتل على قَدْرِ أحوالهم ؛ لأنَّهم فسَّاقٌ ضُلال عصاةٌ أصحاب كبائر عند المحققينَ وأهلِ السنَّةِ ممَّنْ لم يقل بكفرهم منهم ، خلافاً لمَنْ رأى غير ذلكَ ) انتهى (1)
And this was the practice of the first generation regarding them, and there arose in the time of the Companions and after them among the Followers those who held these opinions – from the Qadariyya, the view of the Khawarij, and the Mu'tazila. They did not displace a grave for them, nor did they cut off inheritance from any of them, but they boycotted them, and repelled them with beating, exile, and killing according to their circumstances, because they were sinful, erring, disobedient, people of major sins according to the verifiers and Ahl al-Sunna among those who did not declare them unbelievers, contrary to those who held otherwise.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage provides a historical precedent from the early Muslim community (Salaf) regarding the treatment of followers of deviant sects: the Qadariyya (who denied predestination), the Khawarij (who rebelled against legitimate rulers and declared major sinners kafir), and the Mu'tazila (who emphasized rationalism). The author states that the early generations did not 'displace a grave' for them – meaning they did not remove them from Muslim cemeteries – and did not cut off their inheritance rights, indicating they considered them Muslims in outward legal rulings. However, they did implement a policy of social boycott (hajr) and corporal punishment such as beating, exile, and in extreme cases killing, but only according to the severity of their actions. The author explains that these groups are considered sinful, errant, disobedient, and guilty of major sins (kabā'ir) according to the scholars of Ahl al-Sunna who do not hold them to be kafir. This is in contrast to those who held a stricter view and declared them kafir. This historical account supports the earlier ruling that innovators should be disciplined but not excommunicated.

Key Terms
فساق
كبيرة
بدعة
هجر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf were lenient on heresy and did not punish innovators.
Correction: The passage shows they used harsh physical punishment (beating, exile, killing) while maintaining Islamic legal status (inheritance, burial).

Checkpoint

A) They cut off their inheritance because they were kuffar.
B) They left their inheritance as for any Muslim.
C) They gave their inheritance to the state.
D) They only allowed inheritance if they repented.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf treated followers of deviant sects as Muslims in legal rulings but subjected them to severe disciplinary measures, including boycott, beating, exile, and killing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone with a mistaken belief or innovation, do you tend to cut them off completely or discipline them while still considering them Muslim? How does the Salaf's example challenge your default reaction? What would you need to change to emulate that balance?

This passage shows that the Salaf preserved Islamic legal rights even for those they harshly disciplined. Will you reconsider your stance and work to maintain brotherhood with those you disagree with?

Al-‘Anbari's Deviant View on Taswib in Usul al-Din
Sanusi reports the deviant view of al-‘Anbari and al-Baqillani on taswib of mujtahids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that taswib of all mujtahids in usul al-din is a deviant view opposed to the consensus of the umma.

Core Idea
Declaring all mujtahids correct in usul is innovation.

This lesson presents a specific heretical opinion reported by Imam Sanusi in his commentary. Al-‘Anbari held that every mujtahid is correct in matters of usul al-din that admit interpretation, breaking the consensus of the Muslim community. We also see an extension of this view to non-Muslims who sincerely seek truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the key terms and the names mentioned.
The passage is short but packed with doctrinal significance.
2
Identify the main claim of al-‘Anbari
Find the statement that describes al-‘Anbari's position. What does he say about mujtahids in usul al-din?
He says their statements are 'correct' (taswib).
3
Understand the consensus he opposes
The passage says he differed from 'ijma' al-umma'. Reflect on what the standard Sunni view is regarding error in usul al-din.
In matters of usul, only one mujtahid is correct; the rest are in error but may be excused.
4
Consider the expanded scope
Look at the narration from al-Baqillani. It extends the taswib view to anyone, even non-Muslims, who exhaust their capacity in seeking truth.
This is an even more radical position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذهب العنبري مِنَ المبتدعة إلى تصويب أقوال المجتهدين في أصول الدين فيما كانَ عُرضةً للتأويل ، وفارق في ذلك إجماع الأمة (۳) قالَ القاضي في ( الشفا » : ( وقد حكى القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني مثل قولِ عبيد الله - يعني : العنبري - عن داود الأصبهاني ، قال : وحكى قوم عنهما أنَّهما قالا ذلك في كلَّ مَنْ عَلمَ اللهُ مِنْ حَالِهِ استفراغ الوُسْعِ في طلب الحقِّ مِنْ أهلِ ملَّتِنا أو مِنْ غيرِهم
And al-‘Anbari, among the innovators, went to the position of declaring correct the statements of the mujtahids in the principles of religion concerning what is susceptible to interpretation, and he differed in that from the consensus of the umma. Al-Qadi said in al-Shifa: 'Al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani narrated a statement like that of ‘Ubayd Allah — meaning al-‘Anbari — from Dawud al-Isfahani, he said: and a group narrated from the two of them that they said that concerning everyone whom Allah knows from his situation to have exhausted his capacity in seeking truth from people of our milla or from others.'
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage reports the position of al-‘Anbari, an innovator, who held that the statements of mujtahids in the principles of religion (uṣūl al-dīn) are all correct as long as the matter is open to interpretation. This view differs from the consensus of the umma. Then al-Qāḍī ‘Iyāḍ in al-Shifā narrates that al-Bāqillānī transmitted a similar view from al-‘Anbari and from Dāwūd al-Iṣfahānī: they both said that anyone whom God knows has exhausted his capacity in seeking truth, whether from Muslims or non-Muslims, is excused. This expanded the scope of taswīb to include non-Muslims who sincerely seek truth.

Key Terms
العنبري
تصويب المجتهدين
أصول الدين
استفراغ الوسع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that taswib of mujtahids in furū‘ (branches) applies also to uṣūl (principles).
Correction: This passage clarifies that applying taswib in usul al-din is a deviant view contrary to the consensus of the umma. In usul, only one mujtahid is correct.

Checkpoint

B) Only one is correct
C) They are all wrong
D) They are sinful

Key Takeaway
Al-‘Anbari's position that all mujtahids are correct in usul al-din is a deviant view opposed to the consensus of the umma.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The View of al-Jahiz and Thumama on the Excuse of the Incapable
Sanusi presents the view of al-Jahiz and Thumama on the excuse of the incapable and declares it kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the controversial view of al-Jahiz and Thumama regarding the excuse of the incapable and the ruling of kufr upon anyone who holds it.

Core Idea
Excusing the incapable from divine proof is itself disbelief.

This lesson presents a contentious theological stance attributed to al-Jahiz and Thumama, who argued that many people—commoners, women, simpletons, and blind followers of other religions—are not subject to divine proof due to their lack of reasoning ability. While this might seem merciful, the passage shows that holding such a view is actually kufr by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Familiarize yourself with the exact wording of Sanusi's concise statement. Note the names and the key terms.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the claim
Understand what al-Jahiz and Thumama said about the categories of people and why they thought there is no divine proof against them.
They mention common people, women, simpletons, and blind followers of other religions.
3
Note al-Ghazali's inclination
The text mentions that al-Ghazali inclined towards this view, but a footnote clarifies his actual position; the main text only mentions an inclination.
Be careful not to attribute the view to al-Ghazali definitively.
4
Understand the ruling
The passage declares that anyone who holds this view is a disbeliever, based on consensus. Ask yourself: Why is excusing the incapable so severe?
Consensus here is considered binding.
5
Reflect on implications
Consider how this ruling relates to the broader Aqeedah topic of takfir and the obligation of rational proof.
This shows the importance of affirming divine proof for all accountable individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال نحو هذا الجاحظ وثمامة (۲) ؛ في أنَّ كثيراً مِنَ العامَّةِ والنساء والبُلْهِ ومُقلّدة النصارى واليهود وغيرهم .. لا حُجَّةَ اللهِ عليهم ؛ إذْ لم تكن لهم طباع يمكن معها الاستدلال قال : وقد نحا الغزالي قريباً مِنْ هذا المَنْحَى في كتابِ التفرقة (۳) ، وقائل هذا كافر ؛ بالإجماع على كفرِ مَنْ لم يُكَفِّرْ
And al-Jahiz and Thumama said something similar, to the effect that many of the common people, women, simpletons, and followers of the Christians and Jews and others ... there is no proof of Allah against them, since they do not have natures with which deduction is possible. He said: and al-Ghazali inclined close to this direction in the book al-Tafriqa, and the one who says this is a disbeliever, by consensus on the disbelief of one who does not declare (such a person) a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents the view of al-Jāḥiẓ and Thumāma, who claimed that many people — commoners, women, simpletons, and those who blindly follow Christians and Jews — have no divine proof (ḥujja) against them because they lack the natural disposition (ṭibā‘) for deduction. The text then says that al-Ghazālī inclined towards this direction in his book al-Tafriqa. However, the passage immediately declares that the one who holds this view is a disbeliever (kāfir), by consensus, because they fail to declare such people disbelievers. This shows the severity of excusing those who are capable of reason but fail to use it.

Key Takeaway

Al-Qadi Abu Bakr on Doubting the Disbelief of Christians and Jews
Al-Qadi Abu Bakr argues that hesitating or doubting the kufr of Christians and Jews is itself kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Qadi Abu Bakr rules that hesitating over or doubting the disbelief of Christians and Jews is itself an act of disbelief.

Core Idea
Doubting definitive kufr is itself kufr.

In this passage, al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani presents a sharp ruling: any hesitation or doubt about the disbelief of Christians and Jews is itself disbelief. He bases this on two sources: the revealed texts (tawqif) and the consensus (ijma') of the Muslim community. As you read, notice the logical chain: if the evidence is certain, then opposing or doubting it can only come from a disbeliever.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words set the stage.
The passage ends with (انتهى) marking the end of the quote.
2
Identify the ruling and the proof
Find the explicit ruling: anyone who hesitates or doubts the kufr of Christians and Jews is themselves a kafir. Then find the proof: textual evidence (tawqif) and consensus (ijma') establish their kufr.
The proof follows 'لأن' (because).
3
Understand the logical implication
Al-Qadi argues that hesitation implies belying or doubting the evidence. Ask yourself: why does belying the text make someone a disbeliever?
The author considers this a direct contradiction of certain knowledge.
4
Reflect on the scope
Note that the ruling includes not only Christians and Jews but also 'everyone who departs from the religion of Islam.' Consider why the author broadens the statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحداً مِنَ النصارى واليهود ، وكلَّ مَنْ فارقَ دينَ الإسلام ، أو وقف في تكفيرهم أو شك قال القاضي أبو بكر : لأنَّ التوقيف والإجماع على كفرهم ، فمَنْ وقف في ذلكَ فقد كذَّبَ النصّ والتوقيف أو شك فيه ، والتكذيب والشك فيه لا يقعُ إلا مِنْ كافر ( انتهى )
Any of the Christians and Jews, and everyone who departs from the religion of Islam, or hesitates in declaring them disbelievers or doubts. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr said: Because the textual evidence (tawqif) and consensus (ijma') are upon their disbelief, so whoever hesitates in that has belied the text and the tawqif or doubted it, and belying and doubting it only occurs from a disbeliever. (End)
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani regarding the status of Christians and Jews. The author begins by stating that anyone who hesitates or doubts the disbelief of Christians and Jews—or those who deviate from Islam—falls under this ruling. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr's proof is that both the revealed textual evidence (tawqif) and the consensus of the Muslim community (ijma') affirm their disbelief. Therefore, to hesitate or doubt is effectively to deny or doubt that evidence, which is an act of disbelief itself. The argument follows a logical sequence: the evidence is clear and definitive, so opposition or uncertainty implies rejection of that evidence, and only a disbeliever would reject it. The passage ends with 'End' (intaha), marking the conclusion of the quote.

Key Terms
التوقيف
الإجماع
النص
تكفير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that hesitating over a matter of kufr is a neutral position or a sign of caution.
Correction: According to al-Qadi Abu Bakr, hesitation or doubt about definitive kufr is itself an act of disbelief, as it implies rejection of the clear textual evidence and consensus.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qadi Abu Bakr, what is the status of someone who hesitates in declaring Christians and Jews disbelievers?
A) They are excused due to lack of knowledge
B) They are sinners but still Muslims
C) They are disbelievers
D) Their status is uncertain

Key Takeaway
Hesitating or doubting a matter established by definitive textual evidence and consensus is itself an act of disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever let your heart entertain even the slightest uncertainty about the disbelief of those who reject Islam, thinking it a minor thing? What does this lesson force you to see about the weight of such hesitation?
?
Is there any area of your faith where you allow passive doubt to linger, considering it harmless? How will you now wage war against that inward hesitation after hearing al-Qadi Abu Bakr's decisive proof?
?
When you encounter Muslims who are reluctant to declare the kufr of clear disbelievers, does it bother your conscience? Or have you become comfortable with a 'tolerant' hesitation that this lesson exposes as a danger to iman itself?

The Excuse from Hearing Negative Descriptions
Example and general ruling on the excuse for improper call.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that hearing only negative descriptions of a prophet does not obligate one to investigate, and that such a person is excused like the people of the interval.

Core Idea
Hearing the opposite of truth does not compel inquiry.

The author begins with an example from history: a false prophet named al-Muqanna'. Some people only heard that he was a liar and a fake, which actually turned them away from investigating his claim. This illustrates a key principle: the call to faith must reach a person in a way that prompts reflection, not repulsion. The author then states the general rule: anyone who has not received the call properly is excused.

Guided Path
1
Read the example of al-Muqanna'
Read the first part of the passage where the author gives the example. Notice that the people heard negative descriptions and thus were not motivated to investigate.
This sets up the principle.
2
Understand the principle
The example shows that hearing the opposite of the truth does not stir the incentive for reflection. Reflect on why this matters for the obligation to believe.
3
Connect to the general ruling
The author then states the general ruling: anyone who has not received the call or received it in a way that does not impel inquiry is excused and treated like the people of the interval.
This is the key takeaway from this lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبوة ؛ كما صبياننا أن كذاباً يقال له : المقنع تحدى بالنبوة كاذباً سمع فهؤلاء عندي في معنى الصنف الأول ؛ فإنهم مع أنهم لم يسمعوا صفته . سمعوا ضد أوصافه ، وهذا لا يحرّك داعية النظر والطلب ) . وأنت ترى أن حجة الإسلام مع الجمهور ؛ فإن من لم تبلغه الدعوة ، أو بلغته بوجه لا يحمل على البحث والطلب .. فهو معذور عند الله تعالى ، وحكمه حكم أهل الفترة ، فلعل ما بلغ الإمام القاضي عياضاً خلافُ ذلك وقد تنبَّه العلامة الأصولي البحرُ أبو عبد الله الزركشي لخطورة مقالة القاضي في حق الإمام الغزالي ، فساق عبارته بتمامها في ( البحر المحيط » ( ٢٣٨/٦ ) ثم قال : ( وما نسبه للغزالي غلط عليه ؛ فقد صرّح بفساد مذهب العنبري كما سبق عنه ، وهو بريء من هذه المقالة ، والذي أشار إليه في كتابه « التفرقة » هو قوله : إن مَنْ لم تبلغه الدعوة من نصارى الروم أو الترك أنهم معذورون ، وليس فيه تصويبهم ، والكلام إنما هو فيمن بلغته الدعوة وعاند ، وإنما نبهت على هذا لئلا يغتر به الواقف عليه ) ، وسيؤكد المصنف ذلك بعد انتهاء النقل
قلتُ : والذي أظنُّهُ أنَّ الغزالي رحمهُ اللهُ تعالى إِنَّما ذكرَ في التفرقة » العذرَ في حَقِّ مَنْ بَعُدَتْ بلادُهُ مِنْ بلادِ المسلمينَ ، ولم تصله دعوة النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أصلاً ، أو وصلَتْهُ على غيرِ وجهها ؛ مِنَ النساء والبُلْه ونحوهم
وأَمَّا مَنْ قَرُبَتْ بلادُهُ مِنْ بلادِ المسلمين ، ووصلته دعوة النبيِّ صلَّى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ على وجهها ، وأمكنته معرفتُها مِنَ المسلمينَ . . فالغزالي
( فإنهم على الأعم الأغلب لا يتأهلون للنظر ، وفي حكمهم من ذكره حجة الإسلام بقوله المنقول قريباً : ( سمعوا ضدَّ أوصافه ، وهذا لا يحرك داعية النظر والطلب ) ، وما التمسه الإمام المصنف عذراً للحجة .. هو ما عليه في الواقع ، وهو مذهب إمامه إمام الدنيا محمد بن إدريس الشافعي ، حيث ذكر في ( الأم » ( ٢٥٣/٤ ) : ( فأما من لم تبلغه دعوة المسلمين . . فلا يجوز أن يقاتلوا حتى يُدْعَوا إلى الإيمان ... ( إلى أن قال : ( ولا أعلم أحداً لم تبلغه الدعوة اليوم إلا أن يكون من وراء عدونا الذين يقاتلونا أمة من المشركين ، فلعل أولئك ألا تكون الدعوة بلغتهم ؛ وذلك مثل أن يكونوا خلف الروم أو الترك أو الخزر أمة لا نعرفهم ) ، واليوم كالأمس ؛ فترى بعض المسلمين ممن أقام في غير ديار الإسلام مَنْ يجهل المعلوم من الدين بالضرورة ؛ كتحريم شرب الخمر مثلاً ، فكيف بغير المسلمين ؟! وأقول ثانية : لا تغرَّنَّك سعة الإعلام وانتشاره ؛ إذ حاله كما قال حجة الإسلام : ( وهذا لا يحرّك داعية النظر ) ، فبلوغ الدعوة لا يعتبر إلا بهذا الشرط ، فصورة الإسلام المشوَّهة التي تستطير في الرائي والمذياع وغيرهما من وسائل الإعلام.. كيف تكون داعية لطلب الحقِّ ؟! بل هي داعية للإعراض عنه ، فلا تعجب أن ترى اليومَ مَنْ له حكم أهل الفترة هو الأعم ، ولله سبحانه رحماتٌ خَبَأَها في كل شيء ؛ حتى في الجهل ، فسبحان من وسعت رحمته كل شيء !
Prophethood; as our children [know] that a liar called al-Muqanna' falsely claimed prophethood, so these are in my view like the first category; for although they did not hear his description, they heard the opposite of his descriptions, and that does not stir the incentive for reflection and inquiry. And you see that Hujjat al-Islam (al-Ghazali) is with the majority; for whoever has not been reached by the call, or it reached him in a way that does not impel research and inquiry... he is excused before Allah Almighty, and his ruling is the ruling of the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah). Perhaps what reached Imam al-Qadi 'Iyad is contrary to that. And the great scholar, the ocean of usul, Abu 'Abd Allah al-Zarkashi noticed the gravity of the Qadi's statement regarding Imam al-Ghazali, so he quoted his full statement in 'al-Bahr al-Muhit' (6/238) then said: 'What he attributed to al-Ghazali is a mistake against him; for he explicitly stated the corruption of the 'Anbari school as mentioned before, and he is innocent of this statement. What he referred to in his book 'al-Tafriqa' is his saying: that those Christians of Rome or Turks whom the call has not reached are excused, and that does not mean approving them. The discussion is only about those whom the call reached and they stubbornly rejected. I have only alerted to this so that the one who comes across it is not deceived.' And the author will emphasize that after finishing the quotation.
I say: What I think is that al-Ghazali, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in 'al-Tafriqa' the excuse on behalf of those whose lands are far from the lands of Muslims, and the call of the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not reach them at all, or it reached them in an improper manner; such as women, the mentally deficient, and the like.
As for those whose lands are near Muslim lands, and the call of the Prophet reached them properly, and they were able to know it from Muslims... al-Ghazali [said nothing about them being excused]. For in most cases they are not qualified for reflection, and in their ruling are those whom Hujjat al-Islam mentioned in his statement quoted recently: 'They heard the opposite of his descriptions, and that does not stir the incentive for reflection and inquiry.' And what the Imam, the author, sought as an excuse for the proof... is what is actually the case, and it is the school of his imam, the imam of the world, Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, where he mentioned in 'al-Umm' (4/253): 'As for those whom the call of Muslims has not reached... it is not permissible to fight them until they are invited to faith...' until he said: 'I do not know anyone today whom the call has not reached except those who are behind our enemies who fight us, a nation of polytheists; perhaps the call has not reached them; such as those behind the Romans or the Turks or the Khazars, a nation we do not know.' And today is like yesterday; so you see some Muslims who reside in non-Muslim lands who are ignorant of what is necessarily known of the religion, such as the prohibition of drinking wine, for example; so how about non-Muslims? And I say again: Do not be deceived by the extent of media and its spread; for its condition is as Hujjat al-Islam said: 'This does not stir the incentive for reflection.' So the reaching of the call is only considered with this condition. The distorted image of Islam that spreads on television, radio, and other media... how can it be an invitation to seek the truth? Rather, it is an invitation to turn away from it. So do not be amazed that today you see that those who have the ruling of the people of the interval are the majority. And to Allah are mercies hidden in everything, even in ignorance. Glory be to Him whose mercy encompasses everything!
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on who is excused for not believing due to not receiving the call of Islam properly. The author begins by giving an example: a false prophet named al-Muqanna', where some people only heard negative descriptions of him, which does not motivate them to investigate his truth. Similarly, if someone receives a distorted image of Islam, they are not obligated to seek the truth. The author then states that al-Ghazali (Hujjat al-Islam) agrees with the majority that those who have not received the call or received it in a way that does not prompt inquiry are excused and are like the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah)—those who lived in periods without prophets. The author notes that al-Qadi 'Iyad might have had a different understanding. Then al-Zarkashi corrects a false attribution to al-Ghazali: al-Ghazali only excused those far away like Romans and Turks if the call did not reach them properly, not those who received it and persisted in denial. The author then gives his own opinion, distinguishing between those far from Muslim lands (excused) and those near who received the call properly (not excused). He cites al-Shafi'i's view that those beyond enemy lines who have not heard the call are not to be fought until they are invited. The author extends this to modern times, arguing that even if media spreads a distorted image, it does not motivate reflection, so many people today are still like the people of the interval. The passage concludes by emphasizing Allah's mercy.

Key Terms
النبؤة
الدعوة
أهل الفترة
النظر والطلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that simply hearing about Islam once is enough to obligate belief.
Correction: This passage shows that the manner and quality of the call matter – hearing negative or distorted descriptions does not count.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why were the people who heard about al-Muqanna' not obligated to investigate his claim?
A) They were too far away to know the truth.
B) They only heard negative descriptions that did not motivate them.
C) They were already believers in the true prophet.
D) They were excused because they were children.

Key Takeaway
If the call reaches a person in a way that repels rather than invites inquiry, that person is excused.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you rejected a truth because the first impression you got was negative. How does this lesson reveal your responsibility in seeking knowledge despite initial barriers?
?
Have you ever been the one who presented Islam in a way that repelled others? What does this lesson teach you about the weight of your words?
?
If someone today hears only mockery of Islam, are they excused before Allah? How does this lesson challenge your assumption about people's accountability?

Correcting the Misattribution to al-Ghazali
Correction of a false attribution to al-Ghazali about the excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Ghazali did not excuse all non-Muslims, but only those far away who never received a proper call.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali's excuse is only for the unreached, not the stubborn.

The commentator al-Zarkashi corrects a misunderstanding. Some attributed to al-Ghazali the view that all non-Muslims who persist in disbelief are excused. But al-Zarkashi shows that al-Ghazali explicitly refuted that and only excused those who never received the call or received it improperly. The author adds his own clarification, distinguishing between those whose lands are far and those near who received the call properly.

Guided Path
1
Read the correction by al-Zarkashi
Read al-Zarkashi's full statement. Note how he clarifies that al-Ghazali only excused those whose lands are far, not those who received the call and rejected it.
2
Understand the distinction
Al-Zarkashi emphasizes that al-Ghazali's statement in 'al-Tafriqa' was about those who never received the call, not about those who stubbornly reject after receiving it.
3
Reflect on the author's agreement
The author confirms that al-Zarkashi's correction is accurate and that al-Ghazali is innocent of the false attribution.

Source Text

Misconception & Correction

Checkpoint
According to al-Zarkashi, what was al-Ghazali's actual position in 'al-Tafriqa'?
A) All non-Muslims are excused.

C) Those whose call has not reached are excused; it does not approve their disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says those who received the call and stubbornly rejected are not excused. Reflect on your own response to the truth when it reached you. Are there areas where you have been stubborn despite clear proof? What will you do about it today?
?
Al-Ghazali's careful distinction shows he did not excuse stubborn rejection. How does this challenge your assumptions about who is accountable? Could there be areas where you have been making excuses for your own disobedience? Ask Allah to guide you to truthful repentance.

Modern Application: Distorted Call and Ahl al-Fatrah
Author's distinction, al-Shafi'i quote, and modern application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that even today, many people are excused because the call reaches them in a distorted form that does not prompt inquiry.

Core Idea
A distorted image of Islam can be as effective as no call at all.

The author builds on al-Shafi'i's ruling that those behind enemy lines who have not heard the call are not to be fought. He then applies this to modern times: even with media saturation, if the image presented of Islam is negative and repulsive, it does not actually call to the truth. Such people are like the people of the interval, and Allah's mercy encompasses them.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's distinction
Read the author's clarification: those far away whose lands are distant from Muslims are excused; those near who received the call properly are not necessarily excused.
2
Read al-Shafi'i's ruling
Al-Shafi'i states that those who have not received the call are not to be fought until they are invited. He gives examples of distant peoples.
3
Apply to modern media
The author argues that the distorted image of Islam presented in media today does not invite reflection; it repels. So many are like ahl al-fatrah.
Consider the condition: the call must stir the incentive for reflection.

النبوة ؛ كما صبياننا أن كذاباً يقال له : المقنع تحدى بالنبوة كاذباً سمع فهؤلاء عندي في معنى الصنف الأول ؛ فإنهم مع أنهم لم يسمعوا صفته . سمعوا ضد أوصافه ، وهذا لا يحرّك داعية النظر والطلب ) . وأنت ترى أن حجة الإسلام مع الجمهور ؛ فإن من لم تبلغه الدعوة ، أو بلغته بوجه لا يحمل على البحث والطلب .. فهو معذور عند الله تعالى ، وحكمه حكم أهل الفترة ، فلعل ما بلغ الإمام القاضي عياضاً خلافُ ذلك وقد تنبَّه العلامة الأصولي البحرُ أبو عبد الله الزركشي لخطورة مقالة القاضي في حق الإمام الغزالي ، فساق عبارته بتمامها في ( البحر المحيط » ( ٢٣٨/٦ ) ثم قال : ( وما نسبه للغزالي غلط عليه ؛ فقد صرّح بفساد مذهب العنبري كما سبق عنه ، وهو بريء من هذه المقالة ، والذي أشار إليه في كتابه « التفرقة » هو قوله : إن مَنْ لم تبلغه الدعوة من نصارى الروم أو الترك أنهم معذورون ، وليس فيه تصويبهم ، والكلام إنما هو فيمن بلغته الدعوة وعاند ، وإنما نبهت على هذا لئلا يغتر به الواقف عليه ) ، وسيؤكد المصنف ذلك بعد انتهاء النقل
